Important News

Wang's Telegram Arrives in Ping 101

The Various Parties Were Quite Shocked 102

Zhang Xueliang Felt Extremely Stung After Reading the Telegram

Song, Sun, and Others Spoke Extensively About Wang's Telegram

Zhang and Fang, Jiang, and Hu Visited Zhang Qun in Succession

The Various Political Committee Members in Beiping All Urged Zhang Not to Resign Firmly

Beiping Correspondence: After the publication of the telegrams regarding the resignation of Executive Yuan President Wang Jingwei, various parties in the Beiping area were quite shocked. The following is an investigation into the entire course of events and Zhang Xueliang's definite expressions, recorded as follows:

Tense Atmosphere: Wang Jingwei's resignation telegram arrived in Beiping around 10 PM on the 6th. Zhang Xueliang was at Liu Zhe's private residence, casually chatting with Song Zheyuan, Gao Guizi, Sun Dianying, and others. Secretary-General Wu Jiaxiang brought the original telegram and personally presented it to Zhang. After reading it, Zhang felt extremely stung and immediately revealed a pessimistic attitude. He then passed the telegram to Song and the others to read. Song and the others, prioritizing public security, earnestly offered comfort and engaged in extensive discussion. Some believed it was the beginning of a political storm, an excuse to grandstand unrelated to the situation in North China. Others criticized President Wang for acting so casually. At the same time, there were proposals for the various armies to express their opinions. Song and Sun spoke particularly extensively. However, Zhang Xueliang believed the matter was of great importance and that his subordinates should not speak lightly. Around 12 AM, Zhang personally visited Zhang Qun, Chiang Kai-shek's representative, at the Beijing Hotel for a secret two-hour talk. Zhang Qun immediately telegraphed Nanjing and Wuhan to inquire about the truth and conveyed Zhang's intentions. Around 2 AM, Zhang returned to the Prince Shuncheng Mansion and convened key personnel such as Rong Zhen, Bao Wenwei, Zhu Guangmu, Liu Zhe, Xu Yongchang, Shang Zhen, Yu Xuezhong, Song Zheyuan, Pang Bingxun, Sun Dianying, Wu Jiaxiang, and Zhang Qun, for an all-night meeting. They decided to send a telegram to Wang Jingwei, offering an analysis, and another to Chiang Kai-shek requesting instructions. They also dispatched Bao Wenwei to Wuhan to meet with Chiang and present everything in person. Chiang's telegram was immediately drafted and sent. The telegram was quite lengthy and the wording sincere. The telegram to Wang explained his personal feelings and provided a detailed explanation of defense preparations and fundraising. The wording was quite tactful. The telegram had been drafted but not yet sent, as they planned to discuss it further before sending it. The meeting adjourned around 5 AM on the 7th. On the morning of the 7th, Zhang telegraphed the central government, deployed his subordinates, and prepared for the handover. Bao Wenwei was originally scheduled to fly to Wuhan on the 7th, but was unable to depart due to further consultations with Zhang. At 10 AM on the 7th, Fang Benren, Jiang Bocheng, Hu Ruoyu, and others went to the Beijing Hotel to discuss the matter with Zhang Qun. Together, they telegraphed Nanjing and Wuhan to inquire about everything, report on the situation in the North, and request instructions on the direction.

Political Committee Meeting: The Beiping Political Affairs Committee held a discussion meeting at the Prince Shuncheng Mansion at 5:30 PM on the 7th. Attendees included Zhang Xueliang, Xu Yongchang, Shang Zhen, Fu Zuoyi, Pang Bingxun, Song Zheyuan, Sun Dianying, Zhang Qun, Fang Benren, Jiang Bocheng, Jiang Menglin, Yu Xuezhong, Zhang Zuoxiang, Wang Shuchang, Wang Shuhan, Zhou Zuomin, Xiong Xiling, Lu Dangping, Liu [blank], Tang Yu[blank] (represented by Tan Guohuan), and Han Fuqu (represented by Song Shiyan). As it was a discussion meeting, no chairman was elected. Zhang first reported on Wang's telegram and the content of the reply, expressing his resignation. After lengthy discussion, the committee members all urged Zhang not to insist on resigning, but Zhang's attitude was very firm, and he admitted his past mistakes. As a result, it was decided: (1) Zhang would telegraph Wang, resigning his position. The gist of the telegram to Wang was that after the September 18th Incident, the Northeast fell, and he should take responsibility and resign to apologize to the people. Future political affairs would be handled by the Beiping Political Affairs Committee, and military affairs by the Beiping Military Reorganization Committee. However, during this time of national crisis, President Wang bears the heavy responsibility of national administration and should not suddenly resign due to personal matters. He should immediately withdraw his resignation and continue to be responsible. (2) A telegram would be sent to Wang in the name of the Beiping Political Affairs Committee, explaining the process of requesting financial assistance from the central government. The request was solely due to the financial difficulties in Rehe, and they only requested an allocation of one to two million, not five million per month, nor was it a case of using the guise of resistance against Japan to amass wealth. (3) Tan Guohuan would telegraph Tang Yulin, explaining the truth of the matter and that they would still find ways to assist with Rehe's financial difficulties. (4) The Chief of Staff of the Beiping Pacification Headquarters would issue an order to the various subordinate troops, instructing them to focus on training and not be swayed by rumors.

Financial Issues: According to news from the Beiping Political Affairs Committee, Wang's telegram criticized Zhang Xueliang's financial demands in three aspects: (1) The demand for five million from the Ministry of Finance, with at least two million to be paid first. It is said that this was a decision made by the Political Affairs Committee, and Li Shizeng was publicly elected to go to Nanjing to negotiate. At the same time, Hu Ruoyu was also sent, but Hu has not yet departed. Li met with Wang and Song once and has already set sail for Europe, scheduled to arrive in Hong Kong today or tomorrow. Therefore, it is clear that there was no formal negotiation. (2) The responsibility of the Ministry of Railways to raise two million. The process is said to be quite complex. Initially, the North had a certain urgent need and could not raise funds. The central government was also in dire straits, so it was proposed to allocate two million from a certain deposit of the Beining Railway, which was a transfer in nature. Zhang had initially entrusted Song Ziwen to negotiate with the Ministry of Railways on his behalf. Gu Mengyu had replied that he would help, but after a Zhang surname section chief was sent north once, the discussion suddenly changed. Only 300,000 to 400,000 yuan was approved to be borrowed from the bureau, and it was even said that the ministry needed funds and ordered the previously discussed two million to be remitted to the ministry, which led to some disputes. Recently, Zhang had telegraphed a certain minister about this matter, expressing considerable complaints. It is said that Wang heard about this, hence his decision to resign, but it is uncertain. However, Gu Mengyu's resignation is indeed related to this negotiation. (3) Raising three million to help Rehe. It is said that this was an expression of hope from a certain party and not a request from Zhang. Moreover, it was not a matter of raising funds every month.

Zhang Decided to Resign: The day after Zhang received Wang's telegram, someone met with Zhang Xueliang. According to him, Zhang said that after receiving Wang's telegram, he felt extremely pained and decided to resign. It is said that Zhang himself said that he had felt guilty since the September 18th Incident and had long lost the desire to hold his position, but due to the security of Beiping and Tianjin, he could not arbitrarily resign. Now that he had Wang's telegram, it paved the way for him to leave, how could he not be grateful? However, what he did not understand was that if Wang, as the leader of the party and the state, truly believed that Zhang's presence was hindering the implementation of the government's policies, he could simply issue a clear order to dismiss him to demonstrate his authority. If he believed that Zhang's presence in office was inconvenient for his policies, then a single messenger could order him to resign. Why use a roundabout method, merely losing the government's standing, treating the country's future like child's play? How could the people have faith in the government, and how could they avoid being ridiculed by foreigners? Moreover, many of the cited accusations did not conform to the facts, which was even more regrettable. Zhang also said that his reply telegram to Wang had already been drafted. In addition to defending against the various points regarding financial issues, the above two points were also mentioned. Someone also asked Zhang what he would do after resigning. It is said that Zhang said that for the time being, political affairs would be temporarily handed over to the Political Affairs Committee, and military affairs would be temporarily the responsibility of the Military Affairs Committee. He would also telegraph Chairman Chiang, hoping that Chiang himself could come to Beiping to preside over matters. He was willing to assist as a staff member. If Chiang could not come, he hoped that the government would send a senior official who could take responsibility in the North to Beiping, and he would also do his best to assist. In short, no matter what, he would not cause unrest in the region due to his personal advancement or retreat, adding to his own guilt. He would do his best to ensure that there was no slightest disturbance in the North. (August 8th)

Detailed Information on the Communist Bandits' Incursions 103

Kuang Jixun's Faction is Relatively Strong

The Kong and He Factions Are About to Be Eliminated. Hankou Correspondence: The Communist bandits in Hubei Province include Kuang Jixun in the east, Kong Hechong in the south, He Long in the center, Wang Bingnan in the west, and Cheng Kechun in the north, as well as local bandits, mutinous soldiers, and mixed troops under Wang Tai. The following is an investigation into the incursions of the various factions, with a general overview as follows:

Kuang Jixun's Faction: Among the Communist bandits in Hubei Province, the pseudo-Fourth Front Army has the strongest force, led by the notoriously fierce Kuang Jixun. They have infiltrated the counties in eastern Hubei, and the bandits on the border of Henan and Anhui are in contact with them and are also subject to their control. Most of the bandits are entrenched in Huang'an, and the entire county has been communized. The Soviet of the Hubei-Henan-Anhui Province is located there. A part of their pseudo-25th Army has infiltrated Yaopoling in the north of Guangji County, attempting to unite with the bandits in southern Hubei. Liao Rongkun's division of the pseudo-25th Army is entrenched inside and outside Luotian County, as well as in the Dahe'an, Dongchongfan, [blank]jiashan, and Guijiashan areas, constantly encroaching on the border between Huanggang, Qishui, and Macheng, and attempting to unite with the bandits in Huoshan and Shangcheng counties. The pseudo-9th Division, 25th Division, and Chen Changhao, Xu Bingzhong, Deng Zhigao and other factions of the pseudo-4th Army 11th Division have infiltrated the Kouhe, Weijiadawan, Yaojiaji, Ta'ergang, and Tieshidun areas in Huangpi, attempting to attack the county seat. The pseudo-27th and 28th Divisions have infiltrated Huanggang from Huang'an, including the Zuojiatian, Lijiaji, Cangbu, [blank]Xiaopu, Pan[blank], Sandian, and Sanlifan areas. A part of the pseudo-Fourth Front Army has infiltrated the Qichun, Zhangjiabang, Wangtiantian, and Liugonghe areas. The pseudo-Independent Division Zhang Guotao, and the pseudo-guerrilla Independent Regiment have infiltrated Shunheji, Chengmagang, Xizhangdian, Baifengzui, and Qilipu in Macheng. They besieged the county seat on July 9th and were relieved on the 15th. On the 25th, the bandits from Anyu were added, and they launched a three-pronged counterattack, which was again relieved. At the beginning of this month, they besieged the county seat three times, and there is no confirmed report yet. It is said that the government army has dispatched heavy troops to block and suppress them in various ways and has begun a general offensive. Guangji, Luotian, Huangpi, Qichun, and Huanggang counties are also being suppressed by the stationed troops.

Kong Hechong's Faction: The Communist bandit pseudo-16th Army Kong Hechong faction is infiltrating the counties in southern Hubei. Their nest is in Longgang and Yanxia, which belong to Yangxin County. The two divisions of Kong's department, Zhang Tao and Guo Ziming, constantly infiltrate Daban, Paishi, Sanxikou, Xiaojipu, and Taipingtang. Those in Daye are a part of Guo Ziming and Ji Zhendong's department of the pseudo-9th Division, infiltrating Huayoushu, Bajiaoting, and Fantanpu. Those in Echeng are a part of Guo and the two factions of peasant bandits Zhang Zhi and Zhang Songru, infiltrating Yanglinqiao and Maojiapu. Those in Tongshan are the entire pseudo-16th Army Independent 3rd Division Xu Jinmen, and the pseudo-guerrilla team and Red Guards, entrenched in Fushi, Hengtan, and Sanjiejian. On July 13th, they captured the county seat in six routes, but it was soon recovered by reinforcements, suffering heavy losses and fleeing back to their old nest. Those in Xianning are Ye Jinbo's department of the pseudo-Garrison Division, and the pseudo-guerrilla team and Red Guards, entrenched in Baidun, Chadi Pu, Gaocha Ping, Feiji Dun, and Changbu Tang, attempting to destroy the Xiang-E Railway. Those in Tongcheng are Shen Guozhen and Liu Yongkang's faction of Kong's department, entrenched in the Huangpao Mountain and Matou areas. Chongyang has the pseudo-Independent 2nd Division, and Pubei has the remnants of Xiong Mingjie. The bandits in Chongyang are entrenched in Dayuan'an and the Shalong Bridge of Xiushui. The bandits in Pubei are hiding in Zhongxinpong, Sanshanyuan, and Luoja, and dare not openly harm people. Because the above parts of Kong's banditry are united with the bandits on the border of Hunan and Jiangxi, their momentum is quite large. In fact, Kong's direct subordinates in Hubei are only seven or eight thousand people, and the number of guns is only over three thousand.

He Long's Bandit Faction: The Communist bandit pseudo-26th Army He Long department, under the jurisdiction of the 7th, 8th, 9th, and 3rd divisions, hides between Tianmen, Qianjiang, Jingmen, and Mianyang in central Hubei. Duan Dechang is also his subordinate. That area is the Xiang River basin, and the Diaowen Lake in Hanchuan County on the north bank is its base. Honghu, which belongs to Mianyang, and Qianjiang and other counties on the south bank are also the location of nests. It is estimated that He Ying (female bandit), Peng Guocai, and Duan Dechang are the three factions that harass Mianyang, Honghu, Fengkou, Guomiao Wan, Tuochuanbu, Shahu, Yanglindu, and Magangfu Chang, attempting to attack Tonghaikou. The bandits who harass Tianmen, Yuxinhe, Huibutou, Jingtang, Lushi, Changshou'an, and Huatai are He Long's direct troops and most of Duan Dechang's pseudo-9th Division. Those entrenched in Qianjiang are the pseudo-8th Division and a part of the 9th Division. Jianli is a part of the pseudo-8th Division, the pseudo-guerrilla team, and the Red Guards. The river and streams are the remnants of Yu Huaxin. Jingshan is Duan Yulin's troops, Zhongxiang is a part of the pseudo-9th Division, and Jingmen and Jiangling are the troops of Jiang Shangjian and Gongchen, uniting the local bandits Li Ziqing and Wu Zhifu. This faction has suffered heavy losses after being suppressed by the army. Diaowen Lake, Yuxinhe, Huibutou, and Qianjiang County have been recovered by the government forces. The bandit divisions 8 and 9 have completely collapsed. Only He Long led the Fourth Regiment of the Seventh Division and fled into the Honghu old nest. There are no more than 5,000 bandits. It should not be far from cleaning up and sweeping the courts. In addition, within the area of central Hubei, there are also three factions of communist bandits Hou Yuting, Chen Zhengyu, and Li Tieqing, who constantly harass the Zhurushan, Guojiajing, and Zhengjiaban of Hanyang County, and some of them also harass Xiaosigou and Huanglingji. It is not known whether they are subordinate to He Long.

Wang Bingnan's Faction: The Communist Bandit Pseudo-First Teaching Division Commander Wang Bingnan's faction, and the factions of Hu Di and Zeng Siwen, are entrenched in Badong, Changyang, Wufeng, Hefeng, and Jianshi counties in western Hubei. Wang Bing's troops have more power. Wang is located at the junction of Bachang in Jiangnan, and Hu is located in Qinglong Erxi in Jiangbei. They had repeatedly been searched after the Hou Fang An in Jianshi, and Jiangbei has been recovered. The Jiangnan big faction has also been defeated. They are now all lurking in the mountains and forests and dare not show off again. As for the pseudo

The West Hubei Guerrilla Brigade has infiltrated the Yangjia Yuan, Xindianzi, and Yinjiawan areas of Songzi. After being besieged by the army, they have collapsed and are no longer a force.

Cheng Kechun's Faction: The Cheng bandits are entrenched in the Zhaoyang area. After being broken by Fan Shisheng's troops in northern Hubei many times, their strength was completely lost. Now there are only more than a hundred people and forty or fifty guns. Each faction, Baokang has Li Guangyi and Wei Junbo, Yun County has Zhang Laosi, Wang Lao Jiu, and Hong Longbao, and Yunxi has Li Xingwu and Hong Wuzi.

Zhao Yilin's Faction: In addition to the Communist bandits, local bandits, Henan bandits, and Shaanxi bandits, there are also so-called secret society bandits. This only exists in western Hubei. In Yichang, it is called the Huangxiang Society, and the leader is Zhao Yilin, secretly active in the Wuduhuo Heiyuan Township and other places in the county. In Lichuan, it is called the Badeh Society, and the bandit leader is Duan Wenxiang, with about hundreds of people and more than a hundred guns, constantly harassing Taipingzhen and Zhonglu Street.

Communist Bandit Organization: The places where bandits reach have a wide variety of institutions. In the direction of West Hubei, there is the Central Sub-Bureau, the highest organ commanding the red bandits in the southwest provinces. The governments of Hunan and Hubei provinces are located in Honghu

There are also organizations such as pseudo-Central Branch School, arsenal, hospital, radio station, and customs. The Soviet of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui provinces is located in Shangcheng (southern Henan) and Huang'an. There is a Soviet in Hunan, Hubei, and Jiangxi in Xiushui, (Jiangxi Province) and each county has a county Soviet, the district has a district Soviet, and the township has a township Soviet. There are also land committees, economic committees, anti-suppression committees, comfort teams, peasant mutual aid societies, and children's groups. They are all local ruffians and ignorant people who use spears, knives, and spears as weapons and are used by the Communist bandits. Therefore, their ravages throughout the province and the poisoning of the local area are very fierce. (August 9th)

Anhui Province 104

Jinping County will be established 105

Divide the recovered bandit areas into county areas.

The county seat is located in Jinjiazhai, Liu'an. Anqing Correspondence: Anhui Province originally had sixty counties. Recently, the Provincial Government established Jiashan County in Sanjie Town, the junction of Chuzhou, Lai'an, Dingyuan, and Xuyi counties, and appointed former Provincial Party Committee Li Weitang as the county establishment preparation member. Now, Liao Weipu and other citizens of Liu Duo Brigade have submitted a report to the Provincial Government, requesting the establishment of a new county in the Jinjiazhai area of the county, that is, Jinjiazhai as the new county seat. The northeast is to be filled with the land west of Mabao belonging to Liu'an. The south follows the Dabie Mountain, and the north branches from Baoyun Mountain, Foxiangzhai, and San cengnao, west to Songziguan, as the southeast area of the new county. It is more northward from Songziguan through the Feiqishan of Shangcheng County, Henan Province, along the Jingangtai to Dog Ridge, and transferred to the territory of Gushi County in Henan Province, to reach the southern part of Huoqiu in Anhui, as the northwest area of the new county. In summary, the total area, population, and products of the entire county have the possibility of establishing a new county. The establishment of the new county is directly under the jurisdiction of the Anhui Provincial Government, so as to exercise jurisdiction, so that the remote areas become the hinterland, and the thorns become the open flat. Politics has a center, and suppression is convenient. After receiving the report, the Provincial Government believed that the various sections submitted by the citizens were still factual, and has ordered the Department of Civil Affairs to verify and report. It is also heard that the Provincial Government intends to use the two characters Jinping for the name of the new county. As for the situation in Jinjiazhai, it is more than 200 li north of Huoqiu, 240 li northeast of Liu'an, 180 li west of Huoshan, 180 li south of Macheng in Hubei Province, 130 li northwest of Shangcheng in Henan Province, and more than 200 li from Gushi. The Dabie Mountains run across the borders of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui provinces. The southwest is the source of the Shi River, and the southeast is the source of the Bi River, and Jinjiazhai is located in the middle. In the past, political power was not easy to extend into, causing it to be occupied by Communist bandits. It was also not easy for the counties to suppress it. The provincial army went to aid, but was restricted by the provincial boundary, watching and not advancing, causing harm to this day, and becoming the base of the Communist bandits, almost becoming the abandoned land of the three provinces of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui. This time, the army suppressed, and the area has been recovered, taking the people out of the water and fire, and returning to the seat. If the establishment of the county is realized, then it will not be easy for the Communist bandits to covet it. (August 8th)

The Niu Lan Case 106

Continued Interrogation Proceedings 107

Niu Lan Still Requests Transfer to Shanghai for Trial: The Jiangsu Higher Court continued the trial of Niu Lan and his wife for endangering the Republic of China at 8:00 AM on August 10th at the Jiangning District Court. The trial was still presided over by Li Mian, the presiding judge of the Jiangsu Higher Court, along with judges Yin Rixu and Lin Zemin, prosecutor Zhu, and clerk Wu Daquan. Representatives from various agencies and organizations were present to observe the proceedings. The court session began at 8:40 AM. After the judges took their seats, they ordered the Niu couple to be brought from the detention center. Niu was wearing a beige suit, while Wang Deli had on a black silk Chinese-style cheongsam and Chinese cloth-soled shoes. Their spirits and complexions were better than before the hunger strike. The presiding judge first addressed Niu, stating that the trial would continue today and that he must answer the questions asked. Niu, because the Chen translator could not accurately convey his true intentions, requested that the previous translator, Yang, be present in court. The court approved this request and ordered the bailiff to immediately telegraph for Yang to come to court, and then continued the interrogation. (Presiding Judge asked) Are you 34 years old? What is your nationality? Niu stated that the court could not try the case. If the trial was being conducted under the order of the Ministry of Justice, it was incorrect. (Presiding Judge) If you do not answer, a judgment can be made. (Niu) There are three reasons for transferring the trial to Shanghai: (1) In Shanghai, experts can be hired to authenticate the written records. (2) In Shanghai, reliable witnesses can be found. (3) In Shanghai, reputable lawyers can be hired, and evidence can be photographed. (Presiding Judge) Your previous requests for transfer have been rejected. The jurisdiction has been determined, and this court should conduct the trial. If you want to hire reputable lawyers, any lawyer practicing in this court can be hired. (Niu) Many pieces of evidence reported in the newspapers are not in my own handwriting. This matter should be photographed by a lawyer for record. (Presiding Judge) Since it was not written by you, you can find witnesses. (Niu) I do not wish to hire a Chinese lawyer. I should be allowed to invite Fess to appear in court. (Presiding Judge) There are many reputable lawyers in China. Anyone practicing within this court can be hired. There is no need to hire a lawyer in Shanghai. (Niu) I am not afraid of being judged by an independent body, but I do not want the judicial authorities to joke around. (Presiding Judge) This court has the authority to try this case. Why do you say we are joking around? (Niu) This court is not an independent court, and it does not have jurisdiction over this case. I do not wish to answer, but I declare that, according to Article 301 of the Criminal Procedure Law, I reserve the right to make a final statement. (Presiding Judge) Regarding your three reasons for requesting a transfer: first, you can hire reputable lawyers; second, any evidence can be presented in this court; third, if you have anyone who can authenticate the written records, you can invite them. (Niu) I do not wish to say much now. Please reserve my right to make a final statement. (Presiding Judge) If you do not speak, you can be convicted under Article 310 of the Criminal Law. (Presiding Judge) What is your nationality? (Presiding Judge) Where do you live? (Presiding Judge) What do you do for a living? (Presiding Judge) When did you come to China? (Presiding Judge) Where did you live when you first came to China? (Presiding Judge) After you were arrested, you initially said you were Belgian to the police. Later, when asked, the Belgian consulate said you were not. (Presiding Judge) You also said you were Swiss. When asked, the Swiss consulate also said you were not. From these two points of view, you are a person from a country without a treaty. (Presiding Judge) Your nationality is unclear. If you do not say, then you are a person from a country without a treaty. (Presiding Judge) People from countries without treaties are subject to Chinese law. (Presiding Judge) When did you come to Shanghai? (Presiding Judge) Did you state in the Second Branch of the High Court that you came to Shanghai on March 15, 1919? Is that correct? (Presiding Judge) How exactly did you come to China? (Presiding Judge) Didn't you say that you came from Berlin through Moscow, from Moscow to Harbin, from Harbin to Dalian, and from Dalian to Shanghai? (Presiding Judge) What exactly did you do in Shanghai? (Presiding Judge) You said you came to Shanghai to be a teacher. If you were a teacher, why did you have four residences? (1) 49 Nanjing Road, (2) 74 West Garden, Yuyuan Road, (3) 66 Hart Road, (4) 235 Sichuan Road. (Presiding Judge) Are these four residences all where you lived, or were they your offices, or where Wang Deli lived? (Presiding Judge) If you say you were a teacher, why did you rent so many houses? (Presiding Judge) In your statement to the Second Branch of the High Court, you said you came to Shanghai for business, and only later said you were a teacher. (Presiding Judge) If you were in business, what kind of business did you do? Did you have contact with Chinese people? Who were they? If you were in business, was it personal or a company? Companies have their logos, and individuals also have their marks. (Presiding Judge) You also said that the foreign company was located in Beijing. Beijing is a very large place. Where exactly was it located? What kind of business was it? (Presiding Judge) You previously stated that you were engaged in import and export trade. What kind of trade was it? (Presiding Judge) Looking at it this way, the business you did cannot be explained clearly. It is evident that you were not in business. (Presiding Judge) If you do not answer today, you are hurting yourself. (Presiding Judge) Who is Wang Deli to you? (Presiding Judge) According to you, you are husband and wife. Can you produce a marriage certificate? If you cannot produce a certificate, it is evident that you are not husband and wife. (Presiding Judge) On March 15, the day you were arrested, if you had been honest, why did you throw the Zhaofeng door tickets and car tickets out of the car window? (Presiding Judge) Your residence was discovered in the note thrown from your body. (Presiding Judge) Did you rent the Nanjing Road house yourself? (Presiding Judge) According to you, An Lisheng rented it. Can the person An Lisheng be found now? (Presiding Judge) You said that An Lisheng lived in room C on Nanjing Road. Why can't An Lisheng be found? (Presiding Judge) Pan A'da, who takes care of the house, has testified that you give him four yuan a month to watch the house. (Presiding Judge) When the police arrived, Pan A'da pointed out that An Lisheng was you, and you called him Mr. An Lisheng. (Presiding Judge) The landlord, Ding Jingsheng, said that you also paid the monthly rent, and you called him An Lisheng. (Presiding Judge) If you say that the house was rented by An Lisheng, you should hand over An Lisheng. If you cannot hand him over, since there are testimonies from Pan and Ding, then you are An Lisheng. (Presiding Judge) Three iron boxes were found in the small cabinet. The evidence of your crimes was found in the third box. (Presiding Judge) One box contained evidence of endangering the Republic of China, and another box contained US dollars. (Presiding Judge) You said at the time to the police that there were 1,100 US dollars. After investigation, there were only 823 dollars, and they were sealed in envelopes. (At this point, Niu was looking at the three small boxes repeatedly while listening to the translator.) (Presiding Judge) You said that the money in the box was short, perhaps used by An Lisheng at the time. (Presiding Judge) Now I ask, are the boxes yours? If they are not yours, how do you know there is money inside? (Presiding Judge) At the time, you said that you wanted to take the US dollars in the box to pay the lawyer's fees. (Presiding Judge) If the money is not yours, how can you take it to pay the lawyer's fees? (Presiding Judge) Since you know how much money there is and can dispose of it yourself, then it is evident that the boxes are yours and the money is also yours. (To be continued)

Local Correspondence

Songjiang 108

Motivation for Dredging the City River: Since the beginning of summer, the weather has been extremely dry, and there has been a prolonged drought. The amount of water in the tides has decreased significantly. The city river has not been dredged for many years and has almost become a ditch. Even when there are occasional tides, the water is murky and unsuitable for drinking. The public increasingly feels the lack of water. Wang, a member of the County Executive Committee, proposed at the regular meeting of the committee to dredge the city river for relief. This proposal was forwarded to the county government for handling. After approving the proposal, County Magistrate Shen immediately ordered the First District Office to work with the Construction and Public Security Bureaus to devise a plan and actively carry it out. However, the city river was last dredged in 1914. At that time, in addition to donations, the funds were still far short, and loans were obtained from the financial community. This was handled by the Municipal Office. Later, the accounts were lost and have not been settled. Although the current dredging is essential, how to raise the dredging funds will be decided after the District Office convenes discussions with the Construction and Public Security Bureaus.

Suzhou 109

Provincial Party Headquarters Thoroughly Investigates Party Disputes: The fact that Wu County Party Committee members Zhu Yanliang, Zhou Shanfu, and Liao Yingzhong, among others, were accused by various district party committees of collecting fees from opium dens, gambling houses, and brothels, and of embezzling party funds, has been reported in yesterday's newspaper. It is now known that party member Chen Weizhi was designated by the party committee as a suspected reactionary and was arrested and sent to the Public Security Bureau for interrogation and detention. On the 9th, he was transferred to the province for further investigation. In addition, party member Gao Junxiao was also arrested yesterday morning and temporarily detained in the Public Security Bureau. Yesterday, various district party committees urgently telegraphed the Provincial Party Headquarters to complain about the party committee's arbitrary arrests of party members. Currently, the Provincial Party Headquarters dispatched Lu Baolin to Suzhou on the 9th to investigate the facts. After arriving in Suzhou, Lu investigated the case files and has obtained considerable evidence. Lu also took the opportunity to investigate the case of mutual bribery accusations between the Anti-Japanese Association and the County Party Committee. Party members from various districts of Wu County have been appealing to Lu in person to uphold justice. Lu is scheduled to return to the province on the 10th to report his findings.

Petition to Postpone the Implementation of the Special Construction Tax: The Finance and Construction Bureaus of Wu County, with the approval of the Provincial Department, were scheduled to implement a special construction tax on slaughter tax in Wu County starting on the 16th of this month. However, the Fresh Meat Industry Association, noting that education and other taxes are already levied on the slaughter tax, sent a letter to the Education Association, which forwarded it to the county government, requesting a postponement of the special construction tax.

Wuxi 110

Chambers of Commerce from Various Counties Hold Meeting in Wuxi: The Chambers of Commerce of the counties formerly under the Changzhou Prefecture held a meeting at the Wuxi County Chamber of Commerce on the afternoon of the 9th to discuss the business tax issue. More than 30 people attended, including Lin Junbao and Yu Yicheng from Wujin, Hua Shaochun and Cai Rong from Wuxi, Zhu Zhongjing from Yixing, Wu Shuying from Jiangyin, and Zhu Lifu from Jingjiang. The resolutions on key issues were as follows: (1) Regarding the first of the six opinions proposed by the Chamber of Commerce Federation, requesting a reduction in the tax rate, the Provincial Government did not adopt the opinion of the Higher Chamber of Commerce Federation, which stated that merchants were already finding it difficult to bear the burden. Instead, new regulations were issued, which are too burdensome for merchants. It was resolved to continue to vigorously advocate for the reduction. (2) Articles 8, 20, and 25 of the Provisional Regulations on Business Tax in Jiangsu Province, as well as Chapter 6 on penalties, should be revised. The standards for revision are: (A) Article 8: All businesses should keep an annual total account book, and at the beginning of each business year, allow personnel from the Business Tax Bureau to conduct investigations. (B) Article 20: Please delete the 19 characters "(or those who temporarily establish a main branch or sub-branch at the place of production to purchase goods)". (C) Article 25: Please delete the word "promotion." (D) Chapter 6 on penalties: The original penalties are too severe and should be reduced across the board. (3) Article 21 of the original Regulations on the Collection of Business Tax in Jiangsu Province should be added to the new regulations. (4) Regarding the request from various industries to reduce the tax rate, the Chamber of Commerce Federation should vigorously advocate for it. (5) Oil, salt, firewood, charcoal, coal, and miscellaneous grains are essential daily necessities for the people. Please follow the example of rice and wheat and change the tax to two per thousand. (6) Cotton yarn and wheat are both raw materials for yarn and flour. It is inappropriate to levy taxes on the same item twice, which hinders the principle of unified taxation. Please remove them. (7) Cotton yarn weaving is the raw material for manufacturing daily necessities and has already been subject to unified taxation. When selling, please reduce the tax to two per thousand. The above cases have been sorted out separately and submitted to the joint meeting of the executive and supervisory committees of the Zhenjiang Provincial Chamber of Commerce Federation today (the 11th) for joint discussion.

Strange Murder Case: Coffin Opened for Examination: In the Nanqian Village area of the Eleventh District of the county, Wang, the wife of villager Gu Afu, died suddenly on June 23 while returning home from her mother's house in Dongshantou, after falling into the river at Sushe Bridge, resulting in a strange murder case. Wang Guanshun, the brother of the deceased, reported the incident to the County Court Prosecutor's Office some days ago, requesting an examination and pointing to Zhu Genquan as the murderer. After Prosecutor Shen opened the court, he ordered the bailiff Wu Zixin to go to the countryside and supervise Wang Guanshun, Gu Afu, and others to transport the coffin to the city the day before yesterday. The murderer Zhu Genquan, together with witnesses Zhang and Lu Xiangkun, voluntarily turned themselves in the day before yesterday. Yesterday morning at 11:00 AM, the coffin was opened for examination at the Shengdi Temple in Huishan. Because the corpse had already rotted, it must be steamed today for bone examination to clarify the matter. The coffin has been temporarily handed over to Jiang Zixian, the head of Huishan District, for safekeeping.

Changzhou 111

Anti-Japanese Association Disposes of Confiscated Enemy Goods: The Wuyi Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association convened a meeting on the 9th to discuss the disposal of confiscated enemy goods and resolved: (1) The value of the Hengshuntai enemy goods has been determined to be more than 200 yuan. According to the regulations issued by the province, the goods will be burned, and a penalty of ten times the value will be imposed. (2) The value of the Hengji enemy goods is estimated to be more than 200 yuan. According to the regulations issued by the province, a penalty will be imposed. However, after a thorough search of the county, there is no such store. The carrier, Ding Tong Transport Company, is responsible for handing over the actual name of the disguised store. (3) The suspected enemy goods from Renhe, Dafengren, Yongchang, and Houchang will be handled after identification. (4) A wooden sign will be nailed in front of the stores found to be privately selling enemy goods as a warning. (5) The Transportation Association will be notified that all goods imported hereafter must be reported to the Association first, and unloading can only begin after members are dispatched for inspection. (6) A telegram will be sent to rescue the patriotic compatriot Yun Huifang.

Provincial Committee Comes to Cheng to Investigate Accusations: Li Mutang, the former Director of the First Public Security Bureau, escorted patrol officer Li Chunshan and others to the headquarters on July 13, accusing them of six charges. Conversion of Copper Coins to Silver Dollars Resolved: The dispute over the conversion of copper coins to silver dollars for the public funds stored by the Nantong Education Bureau has been ongoing for a long time. and both principal and interest would be settled together.

The agencies using county funds will jointly organize a clearing

office to increase revenue.

Xiaoshan 117

Tragic News of Entire Family Dying from Plague: The weather in Xiaoshan has been extremely hot recently, and the plague is rampant. Xu Qilong, a resident of Chaijiawu in the western countryside, had his wife Lai die of the plague on the morning of the 6th. On the morning of the 7th, his eldest son returned home from the fields and also contracted the plague, dying by noon. On the 8th, his youngest daughter and youngest son felt feverish and had difficulty speaking, and they also died one after another in the afternoon. On the morning of the 9th, Qilong, whose family of four had all died within three days, went to his relatives' house in Kongjiafen, but suddenly lost consciousness midway. He rushed back home and died within five hours. It is truly tragic news.

A Record of the South China Team's Expedition 122

Promoting National Prestige and Patriotism Among Overseas Chinese

| Li Huitang and Chen Zhenhe Lead Separate Teams | The South China and Hong Kong Football Teams, strong forces from our nation, have been touring and competing in various overseas locations. Wherever they go, their reputation spreads far and wide, and they are deeply loved by overseas Chinese. Here is a summary of the recent performances of both teams, to satisfy the thirst of football fans at home.

South China Loses to Itini

The Result is Two to Three After defeating the Long Xuan team by a score of three to zero, the South China team's reputation for invincibility spread far and wide. On July 19th, they competed against the Itini team, the current champion of Bandung.

An Unintentional Loss At 4:30 PM, the signal was given, and both teams launched fierce attacks. Within just one minute, Itini's right winger, Horal, dribbled the ball along the side, deep into South China's left defense. He then kicked the ball sharply towards the center, and unintentionally, the ball landed in the left corner of the goal. Goalkeeper Zhou noticed and tried to save it, but the ball

hit the post and bounced in. South China unfortunately conceded the first goal.

Illegal and Invalid Itini scored a lucky goal, but fortune did not favor them. Li Huitang took the lead, broke through the defense, and entered the street to knock on the gate. Seeing that reinforcements were not arriving, the opposing goalkeeper rushed out to meet him, but was dodged by General Li, who shot straight at the goal. At that moment, Li Yichen was eager to win and illegally entered the area. The referee ruled that he was offside, and the goal was disallowed. The first half ended with a score of zero to

one against South China.

Beyond Imagination In the second half, the attacks and defenses became even more intense. Not

one minute later, the opposing left winger sneaked in and passed the ball to the center. Chen, the right defender, did not defend with his life and was struck in the chest by the opposing right inside, resulting in another goal. South China's reputation for invincibility began to shake. They launched attacks on all fronts to regain lost ground. Li Yichen made a significant contribution, scoring one goal. Li Huitang directed the entire army, penetrating deep into enemy territory. Li scored with a ground shot, making it two to two.

Lost Due to Penalty Kick After the tie, our army's momentum increased even further.

The opposing team was under pressure from both sides, and it seemed likely that we would turn the tie into a victory. Li Huitang, with the help of Ye Beihua, made a solo run, dodging all the defenders. The opposing goalkeeper rushed out to meet him, but Li cleverly outmaneuvered him, gently sending the ball towards the right corner of the goal. However, the ball moved slowly due to the mud, and was eventually saved by the opposing team. Subsequently, South China was in trouble, and Tan Jiangbai touched the ball with his hand while clearing it, resulting in a penalty kick. The kick was successful, and the result was two

to three, a loss.

After the Hong Kong team regained the lead, victory seemed within their grasp. As soon as the ball was restarted, they surrounded the Japanese team again. Before long, they scored another goal, turning the tie into a victory. Suddenly, their defense was exposed, and the opposing team took the opportunity to score, making it two to two again. Public Swimming Competition 124

Scheduled for August 20th Divided into Adult, Children, and Women's Groups

The annual public swimming competition of the Chinese YMCA on Sichuan Road will be held again soon. The events for the adult group will be in accordance with the regulations of the Far Eastern Games (except that the YMCA swimming pool is measured in yards, so meters will not be) used. The events for the children's and women's groups will be slightly easier, in order to

arouse the interest of newcomers, gain experience through competition, and encourage competition among those who are already familiar with the sport, and improve skills through competition. The brief competition regulations of the YMCA are attached below: (1) Registration: From now until August 18th, at the YMCA Sports Department on Sichuan Road (registration fee: two cents). (2) Competition Date: August 20th at the YMCA swimming pool on Sichuan Road. (3) Events: (A) Adult Group: (1) 50-yard freestyle; (2)

100-yard freestyle; (3) 400-yard freestyle; (4) 100-yard backstroke; (5) 200-yard breaststroke; (6) 1500-yard freestyle; (7) 200-yard relay (5 people per team); (8) Fancy diving. (B) Children's and Women's Groups: (1) 40-yard freestyle; (2) 40-yard backstroke; (3) 40-yard breaststroke; (4) 100-yard freestyle; (5) 80-yard

relay (4 people per team); (6) Fancy diving. (4) Participation: Each person may participate in up to three events. (5) Awards: First place in each individual event will receive a silver shield. First and

second place in each event will receive gold and silver honorary medals.

Tapping the Bell at the Ancient Temple – Records from the Buchengtingsaozhai Studio 133

(71)

78. The ancient temple is, after all, a strange thing. Gradually, it attracted the attention of the people in the city. Some people initially came to see the scenery, but suddenly discovered this strange thing, just like Columbus discovered the New World. They told others, spreading the word from one to ten, and from ten to a hundred, so that visitors came in an endless stream, making me busy all day with boiling water, making tea, and receiving guests, sweating profusely. I am not afraid of sweating, but what I fear is that my sweat will be shed in vain. The way they glanced at the flowers from horseback was to treat our ancient temple as the Great World for fun. I wanted to take the opportunity to talk to them about the meaning of various activities, so that they would take some seeds and scatter them elsewhere. Who knew that I would always be disappointed? They always asked me, "How many students do you have here? How many teachers are there? What is the annual budget?" My tongue followed me and was not very comfortable, having to answer these monotonous and uninteresting words all day long.

Today was an unprecedented day. An economics PhD, Mr. Tang, came. Hearing that we were running a rural work-study program, he came specially to visit. He asked in great detail, and I answered with great enthusiasm. It was truly a pleasure. My tongue can be considered happy today; it has more than compensated for many days of futility. Finally, Dr. Tang gave me a shocking question: "Now is a world of machines. Things made by machines are cheap and good. Handicrafts can never compete with them. You want to grow your own cotton, spin your own yarn, weave your own cloth, and make your own cotton clothes to wear. This is indeed a beautiful ideal, but relying on the power of your ancient temple alone, you can only do wooden machine handicrafts. How can you compete with machine-made products? Machine-made products are cheap and good, while yours are expensive and rough. How can you sell them? Handicrafts are crushed by machines. How can you promote them? The ancient temple should lead farmers to learn from foreign countries head-on. Learning from foreign countries means learning the latest machines from foreign countries. How can you go backwards?" I was stunned by Dr. Tang's question, simply defeated by it. It doesn't matter. This is a good opportunity for me to learn. I have never been so embarrassed as I am today. I believe that the more embarrassed I am, the more substantial my progress will be. Mr. Zhu's and Dr. Tang's views are diametrically opposed. One of them must be wrong. I must quickly invite Mr. Zhu to come so that they can have a debate. No matter who is right, I will always gain some knowledge. (Dr. Tang, please sit for a while. I will go and find Teacher Zhu to talk to you.)

Wang Jingwei's Secret Whereabouts 134

Yesterday, a Representative Was Sent to Wuhan to Meet Chiang

The Political Situation Suddenly Becomes Depressed, and All Parties Are Planning Solutions

Song Ziwen States That Chiang Still Insists on Resolutely Persuading Wang to Remain as President of the Executive Yuan. After Wang Jingwei resigned from his position as President of the Executive Yuan, due to the nature of a responsible cabinet, the heads of the various ministries and commissions of the Executive Yuan also jointly resigned. As of yesterday, the Central Government had not yet issued any statement. Wang moved out of Noel Hospital the night before last, and his whereabouts are extremely secret. Song Ziwen, He Yingqin, and others did not meet with him yesterday. Therefore, the political situation has shifted from a major upheaval to a state of depression. The realization of new developments will still require a considerable amount of time. Chiang Kai-shek, Chairman of the Military Affairs Commission, sent another telegram to Wang, earnestly urging him to stay and hoping to choose a place to meet in person to discuss everything. Wang sent his secretary, Tang Youren, by plane to Wuhan at 8:00 AM yesterday to represent Wang in meeting with Chiang and to explain the difficulties of his resignation. Tang is scheduled to return to Shanghai by plane at 3:00 PM today to report back. It is rumored that Chiang telegraphed Song to go to Nanjing immediately to maintain government affairs. This reporter met with Song yesterday, and Song denied this rumor, saying that he would not go to Nanjing for the time being. The details are recorded below:

The Central Government Has Not Yet Made a Statement. The Central Government Has Not Yet Made Any Statement Regarding the Joint Resignation of the Heads of Various Ministries and Commissions of the Executive Yuan. According to Mayor Wu, a telegram of consolation will be sent to Shanghai within the next few days, earnestly requesting the heads of various ministries and commissions of the Executive Yuan to return to their posts and jointly shoulder the heavy responsibilities.

Chiang Sends Another Telegram to Wang Urging Him to Stay. Since Receiving Telegrams of Resignation From President Wang and the Heads of Various Ministries and Commissions, Chairman Chiang of the Military Affairs Commission Originally Intended to Come to Shanghai Immediately to Personally Request Them to Return to Nanjing and Resume Their Posts. However, Because of His Involvement in Military Affairs of Suppressing Bandits, He Could Not Leave Wuhan. Therefore, He Specifically Telegraphed Wang, Earnestly Requesting Him to Go to Wuhan Immediately to Discuss Everything in Person. After Receiving This Telegram the Day Before Yesterday, Wang Sent Tang Youren, Secretary-General of the Central Political Conference, to Wuhan Yesterday Morning to Represent Wang in Meeting with Chiang.

Tang Youren Flies to Wuhan Yesterday. Tang Youren Went to Longhua Airport at 8:00 AM Yesterday Morning and Took a China National Aviation Corporation Plane to Fly From Shanghai to Wuhan to Meet with Chiang. It Is Said That Chairman Chiang Summoned Wang to Wuhan to Discuss the Issue of Wang's Return to His Post, and It Is Understood That Tang Is Scheduled to Return to Shanghai at 3:00 PM Today.

Wang's Whereabouts Are Secret. On the Evening of the Eighth, Wang Moved From His Residence on Rue Bourgeois to Noel Hospital on Avenue Joffre to Avoid Guests. It Is Now Learned That Wang Moved Out of the Hospital the Night Before Last. As for Where He Moved To, It Is Very Secret, and Outsiders Have No Way of Finding Out. According to Wang's Entourage, Wang Left Shanghai the Night Before Last to Rest in a Quiet Place. This Reporter Asked Mayor Wu About This Matter Yesterday, and Wu Denied It, Saying That Wang Is Still Staying in Shanghai, but His Residence Is Very Secret. It Was Also Learned That Key Figures From the Central Government and Mayor Wu Tiecheng Originally Intended to Meet with Wang Yesterday Afternoon to Persuade Him to Stay, but Wang's Attitude Remains Firm, and His Whereabouts Are Secret, so They Have Not Been Able to Meet With Him. According to Wang's Residence, Wang Left Shanghai Last Night to Rest Elsewhere. Wang Has Refused to See Guests for the Past Two Days, and There Is Also Considerable Doubt That Wang Has Left Shanghai for Another Place. According to Mayor Wu, Although Chairman Lin Has Telegraphed Wang to Go to Lushan for a Meeting, Mr. Wang Stated That He Is Unwilling to Start His Journey Until the Central Government Approves His Resignation. Therefore, It Can Be Concluded That Wang Will Still Stay in Shanghai in the Next Few Days and Will Definitely Not Go Elsewhere.

Opinions of Various Central Committee Members. Central Committee Members Ju Zheng, He Yingqin, Wu Tiecheng, and Others in Shanghai Believe That Wang's Attitude Is Firm, and the Heads of Various Ministries and Commissions Have Also Submitted Their Joint Resignations. They Fear That the Delay Will Be Too Long, Which Will Hinder the Progress of Central Government Affairs. After Discussions Over the Past Two Days, They Decided to Proceed Separately to Find a Solution. That Is, on the One Hand, They Will Try to Find an Appropriate Solution to the Northeast Problem, and on the Other Hand, They Will Do Their Utmost to Persuade President Wang to Stay, So That He Will Return to His Post. In Addition to This, the Central Government Has No Other Options. The Rumor That Zhang's Resignation Was Approved First Is Not Accurate. According to Wang's Entourage, Wang's Entourage Told the Far Eastern News Agency Reporter Yesterday That Mr. Wang Believes That the Resignation of the Heads of Various Ministries and Commissions Is a Common Practice in a Responsible Cabinet System and Has Nothing to Do With Him Personally. Since Mr. Wang Resigned in Anger at Zhang's Non-Resistance, He Has His Own Unavoidable Difficulties and Cannot Abandon His Intention to Resign Simply Because of the Joint Resignation of the Heads of Various Ministries and Commissions. As for Whether the Political Situation Can Make Progress, It Depends on Whether the North China Issue Can Be Dealt With Appropriately.

Song Ziwen's Remarks. At About 5:00 PM Yesterday Afternoon, This Reporter Met With Finance Minister Song Ziwen. According to Song, the Central Government Has Not Yet Replied to the Joint Resignation of the Heads of Various Ministries and Commissions. He Himself Will Not Go to Nanjing for the Time Being or Leave Shanghai for Another Place. Chiang Still Insists on Resolutely Persuading Wang to Stay. As for How the Political Situation Will Develop, All Parties Are Still Exchanging Opinions. The Reporter Asked Whether the Central Government Was Prepared to Elect a New President of the Executive Yuan and Reorganize the National Government Since Wang's Intention to Resign Was Extremely Firm. Song Replied That He Was Not in a Position to Express Any Opinion.

Song Ziwen 135

Refutes the Absurd Theory of a Buffer State 136

Corrects the Views of the London Times' Tokyo Correspondent. Shanghai, September 9th (Reuters) - The London Times' Tokyo correspondent published a theory that the Three Eastern Provinces should be a buffer state between China and Japan. Today, a Reuters reporter met with Finance Minister Song Ziwen, and Song expressed his astonishment at this theory. He said that the strait between Japan and the Asian continent is many times wider than the strait between England and the European continent. England has not been invaded for thousands of years because of the strait, but Japan believes that it is necessary to annex Korea. Japan's procedures for annexing neighboring countries' land are still in progress. Having forcibly seized the Three Eastern Provinces, it is now said that they are advancing on Rehe Province, the gateway to Peiping. The theory of contiguous land has no limits. An English politician said this long ago. The idea of the Three Eastern Provinces as a buffer state, which is recognized by the London Times' Tokyo correspondent, is astonishing. Even a child knows the puppet nature of the "Manchukuo" independent state. It is truly incomprehensible that some people in England have no feeling and do not know how to stop the Nine-Power Treaty, which solemnly and unconditionally guarantees China's territorial and administrative integrity, from being wantonly violated by major powers, but instead want to find a reason for their own inaction. Song also said that the current serious situation, which was caused by Wang Jingwei's resignation, is not surprising and should not be seen as evidence of China's instability. Japan, the invading country, has even experienced the assassination of two prime ministers, one ambassador to China, and one minister of finance because of the Sino-Japanese issue. It is a natural inevitability that China, in a time of national crisis, will experience emotional outbursts due to differences of opinion on the policies and methods of resisting foreign aggression. He is confident that the current situation can be resolved satisfactorily and that the crystallization of public opinion can be obtained to reject the continued invasion of land with the strength of the entire nation, regardless of the cost. China has been extremely patient under extreme provocation, but the advice of European rulers not to escalate the situation has only resulted in China losing a lot of land without firing a single shot.

There Are Still Many Japanese Goods Entering and Exiting 138

Secret Smuggling by Unscrupulous Merchants. Since the Activities of the Blood Pledge Corps, the Transport of Japanese Goods to the Yangtze River Has Been Severely Affected. However, Unscrupulous Merchants Are Still Designing in Every Way to Secretly Smuggle Them. The Recent Situation of the Entry and Exit of Inferior Goods Is Recorded Separately Below:

Large Quantities of Piece Goods Shipped Out. Unscrupulous Merchants in Hankou, Changsha, Yichang, and Other Places Are Purchasing Japanese Piece Goods in Large Quantities Because of Their Price Drops. However, Given the Intense Boycott in Shanghai, These Merchants Are Colluding With the Japanese to Avoid Using Chinese Customs Declarations and Instead Have the Japanese Declare the Goods Themselves. It Is Confirmed That the Night Before Last (the Eighth), 3,000 Pieces of Japanese Piece Goods Were Loaded Onto Japanese Riverboats From Lighters by the Japanese. Therefore, Japanese Piece Goods Can Still Be Sold Unimpeded on the Upper Reaches of the Yangtze River.

Change Packaging and Mail to the Interior. There Are Also Some Unscrupulous Merchants Who Collude With Cotton Weaving Factories to Cut Off the Machine Ends of Inferior Piece Goods and Re-Weave Them With Domestic Brand Names. Because They Cannot Declare the Goods Publicly, They Change the Inferior Goods Into Packages and Mail Them to the Interior. Many Have Already Been Mailed. Jardine Matheson in Chongqing Received a Warning Letter With Bullets Attached. Jardine Matheson Immediately Issued a Statement Saying That the Goods Declared by This Firm Are All Destined for Treaty Ports and That There Are Customs Records That Can Be Examined. This Firm Has Refused to Declare Inferior Goods for Many Years. As for the Talk of Changing the Packaging and Mailing the Goods to Pose as Domestic Goods, That Is Not a Matter for This Firm, and This Firm Has No Right to Interfere. It Should Be Requested That Your Corps Investigate in Detail to Avoid Misunderstandings.

Japanese Goods Still Arriving in Shanghai. The Arrival of Japanese Goods Has Not Stopped Due to the Boycott. They Are Still Being Shipped in Constantly, but Most of Them Are Stored in Warehouses at Various Wharves. The Japanese Ship Asama Maru Has Arrived With Many Inferior Goods, Mostly Piece Goods, but the Exact Number Is Unknown. Only Customers Who Pick Up the Goods Are Allowed to View the Hatch Manifest. Loading and Unloading Are Also Stricter Than Usual.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Committee 140

Re-Examine the Abolition of Taels and the Change to Yuan 141

Recommend That Zhu Wenqi Prepare a Draft Opinion

Submit to the Third Committee Meeting for Review. The Research Committee on the Issue of Abolishing Taels and Changing to Yuan, Organized by the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Convened Its First Meeting at 1:00 PM Yesterday to Continue Discussing the Opinions Expressed by Various Industries on This Issue and to Refer to the Letters From Various County Chambers of Commerce. The Details Are Recorded Below:

Research Committee Meeting. Committee Members Fang Jiaobo, Zhu Wenqi, Chen Zheqing, Luo Qinghua, Lu Wenshao, and Others Were Present. Zhu Wenqi Chaired the Meeting. First, the Chairman Distributed a Compilation of the Various Questions Received From All Parties Regarding the Abolition of Taels and the Change to Yuan for the Second Time for the Committee Members to Study. After a Long Discussion, It Was Resolved That: (1) After Summarizing the Opinions Put Forward by All Parties in Sequence, a General Abstract Should Be Made According to the Topic for Reference; (2) Regarding All Opinions Resulting From This Association's Research, Committee Member Zhu Wenqi Was Recommended to Prepare a Draft Based on the Main Ideas Proposed by the Sugar Industry and Other Eleven Trade Associations and Submit It to the Next Meeting for Review; (3) The Third Committee Meeting Was Scheduled to Be Convened on August 15th.

Wang Yansong's Remarks. A Reporter From the New Sound News Agency Visited Wang Yansong, a Standing Committee Member of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and Chairman of the Silk Industry Bank, Yesterday to Ask for His Opinion on the Abolition of Taels and the Change to Yuan. According to Him, the Issue of Abolishing Taels and Changing to Yuan Is About to Move From Research to Implementation. He Was Previously Recommended by the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to Attend the Research Committee Convened by the Central Bank, but He Was Unable to Accept the Recommendation Due to a Trip to Qingdao. Committee Member Ma Jiliang Attended Instead. As for His Own Position on This Issue, He Believes That the Abolition of Taels and the Change to Yuan Is Indeed a Prerequisite for Unifying the Currency System, but Unifying the Currency System Is Not Something That Can Be Achieved by the Abolition of Taels and the Change to Yuan Alone. After the Abolition of Taels, the Government and Society Must Work Together to Seek the Stability and Improvement of the Financial System, and Only Then Can the Benefits of the Abolition of Taels Be Seen. Although Various Industries Have Different Views on This Issue Now, They Are All in Agreement on Supporting It. Even the Qian Industry Only Advocates Cautious Follow-Up and Does Not Fundamentally Oppose It, Nor Is It for Its Own Selfish Interests. Therefore, the Qian Industry Has Abolished the Increase or Decrease of Two and a Half Hairs, Which Can Also Show Its Selflessness and Impartiality. As for the Exchange Rate Between Taels and Yuan, Which Is Most Common in Commerce, It Should Be a Way for Both Parties to Benefit Equally to Avoid Bias. The Minting of New Coins Must Be in Accordance With the Stipulated Weight and Packaging, and There Should Be No Shortages. A Supervisory Committee Should Be Organized by Various Public Organizations to Supervise and Test Them at Any Time. The Issuance of Exchange Certificates Should Be Publicly Inspected and Made Perfect to Reduce Malpractice. In Short, Everything Will Come Naturally When Conditions Are Ripe. The Public Is Right to Pay Close Attention to This Matter, Which Is Related to the Interests of Society.

Opinions Received Continuously From Various Industries. The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Continues to Receive Opinions Expressed by Various Industries as Follows: (A) The Egg Industry Advocates: (1) The Weight of the New Silver Coin Should Be Based on the Weight of the National Currency Before May, Which Is 7 Maces and 2 Fen. The Purity Should Be at Least 91% Silver, That Is, at Least 6.52 of the 7 Maces and 2 Fen Should Be Pure Silver; (2) The Exchange Ratio Between Silver Taels and Silver Coins Should Be Based on 7 Maces and 2 Fen; (3) A Special Treasury Should Be Established to Unify Issuance, as Advocated by the Qian Industry. The Reserve Fund Should Be at Least 60% Cash and Should Not Be Offset by Other Business Funds. All Industries Should Be Allowed to Inspect It Publicly; (B) The Firewood and Charcoal Industry Advocates: (1) For the Unification of Hard Currency, the Government Should Abolish the Mints in Various Provinces and Return Them to the Central Mint for Minting. The Weight and Purity Should Be in Accordance With the Regulations of the Third Year of the Republic of China. Old Coins Should Be Recalled and Melted Uniformly. There Should Only Be One Type of Silver Coin Circulating Throughout the Country; (2) The Most Important Thing for Soft Currency Is Unified Issuance. The Government Should Set Up a Special Issuance Bureau, and the Issuance Rights of All Ordinary Banks Should Be Abolished. On the One Hand, the Reserves Should Be Replenished So That Ticket Holders Can Redeem Them Anytime, Anywhere; (3) Commercial and Civilian Organizations Have the Right to Supervise and Inspect. They Can Test the Purity of Hard Currency and Inspect the Reserves of Soft Currency; (C) The Clock and Watch Industry Expresses General Agreement, but Has No Comments to Make on the Questions Asked; (D) The Rice Grain Selling Industry Advocates: (1) The Weight of Minting New Coins Should Still Be Based on 7 Maces and 2 Fen. The Purity Should Be Based on the Average Amount of the Original Coins to Show Uniformity; (2) The Exchange Ratio of Silver Taels Can Be Determined According to the Closing Price of Foreign Cents for the Last Three Days, or It Can Be Publicly Agreed Upon by the Chamber of Commerce Together With the Silver Money Industry and Other Relevant Groups to Determine a Moderate Exchange Rate. The Purity of New Silver Coins Should Be Publicly Tested, and the Reserves of Paper Money Should Be Publicly Inspected. A Supervisory Organization Should Also Be Established; (E) The Embroidery Industry Advocates: (1) The Weight of Silver Coins Should Be in Accordance With 7 Maces and 2 Fen of Treasury Silver, and the Purity Must Be No Less Than 90% Pure Silver; (2) The Exchange of Taels and Yuan Relates to Creditors and Debtors in Various Places and Should Be Convened Separately by the Provincial Finance Departments and County Chambers of Commerce and Representatives of the Silver Money Industry to Deliberate and Determine the Situation; (3) After the Above Measures Are Established, on the One Hand, the Administrative Agencies Should Issue Announcements, and on the Other Hand, the Silver Money Industry Should Separately Notify the Debtor and Creditor Customers of Deposits and Mortgages, So That Everyone Will Know About It; (F) The Shipping Industry Association Agrees in Principle, and the Measures Should Be Carried Out Carefully.

Letters Received From Various Local Chambers of Commerce. The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Sent Telegrams to Various Local Chambers of Commerce to Solicit Opinions on This Issue and Has Now Received Letters in Reply as Follows: (A) The Chongming County Chamber of Commerce Advocates: (1) The Weight and Purity of Silver Coins Should Be Based on the Regulations of the Third Year of the Republic of China as a Minimum Standard, With Particular Attention Paid to the Unification of the Currency System; (2) When Silver Coins Are Manufactured, Representatives Should Be Recommended by the Silver Money Industry Association and the Municipal and County Chambers of Commerce to Supervise at All Times; (3) There Should Be a 60% Cash Reserve for the Issuance of Banknotes, and the Remaining 40% Must Have a Reliable Credit Guarantee; (B) The Jiangyin County Chamber of Commerce Advocates: (1) The Weight and Purity of New Coins Should Be in Accordance With the Regulations of the Third Year of the Republic of China and Should Not Be Reduced. Public Testing Should Be Conducted, and a Committee Should Be Established for Long-Term Supervision; (2) The Exchange Ratio Varies From Place to Place. Financial Experts From Major Commercial Ports Throughout China Should Be Gathered to Discuss It at Length; (3) All Provincial Mints Should Be Closed Down, and All Machinery Should Be Concentrated in Shanghai Factory for Manufacturing and Issuance to Achieve Unification. All Banks Must Prepare in Accordance With the Law and Must Not Issue Banknotes Indiscriminately; (C) The Shaoxing County Chamber of Commerce Advocates: (1) The Purity Should Be in Accordance With the Regulations of the Third Year of the Republic of China, and the Weight Should Be 7 Maces and 2 Fen; (2) It Should Be Based on the Average of the Highest and Lowest Prices Within Three Years; (3) The Hard Currency Should Not Be Changed According to the Regulations of the Third Year of the Republic of China, and Society Will Naturally Trust It; (D) The Wujin County Chamber of Commerce Advocates: (1) The Weight and Purity of New Silver Coins Should Be Strictly Minted in Accordance With the Regulations of the Third Year of the Republic of China and Actively Recalled Old Coins to Maintain the Unity of the New Coins; (2) The Silver Foreign Exchange Differs From Place to Place and Should Be Collected by the Local Chambers of Commerce From Various Industries to Make a Fair Exchange in the Regulations, Based on the Actual Value of the Above New Coins; (3) After the Change to Yuan, in Order to Make Society Understand and Believe, (1) The Minting of New Coins Must Be Absolutely Unified; (2) Public Testing; (3) Unified Issuance Rights; (4) Full Reserves, Stipulating That Cash Must Be at Least 60% or More.

Japanese Naval Commander 153

Addresses Subordinates Before Inspection Tour 154

Assistance for the Attack on Rehe

Naval Inspection Tour for Pacification

The commander of the Japanese Third Fleet stationed in Shanghai, Sakonji, originally scheduled to begin his inspection tour of the Yangtze River Japanese warships' defenses on the 11th of this month (today). However, after receiving a telegram from the Kwantung Army on the 7th of this month, deciding to invade Rehe, he immediately convened a joint meeting of naval officers in Shanghai on the evening of the 8th and decided to move the date of the inspection tour forward by one day. Therefore, Sakonji departed on the flagship Izumo at 4:30 PM yesterday to Wuhan, carrying an additional 500 special marines to supplement the shortage of Japanese naval forces along the Yangtze River. His intentions are difficult to fathom. However, according to information obtained by a Shih Wen News Agency reporter, Sakonji summoned Marine Corps Commander Sugisaka and others at the naval headquarters on Jiangwan Road at around 10:00 AM yesterday for a farewell address. In addition to temporarily transferring his duties as naval commander to Sugisaka, he also gave important instructions to his subordinates. The gist of it was: "The important principle of my inspection tour of the Yangtze River defenses this time is to pacify naval officers and soldiers in various places and arouse their patriotic conscience. Because our army (Sakonji's self-designation) in the Northeast has decided to attack Rehe and eliminate the volunteer army on the Chinese side. Although Shanghai is far from Rehe, we must also actively provide sympathy and assistance to the army in the Northeast. My inspection tour will last for about one month. Please take care of Shanghai affairs temporarily, Mr. Sugisaka. After my departure,

you must work harder on protecting our expatriates."

Report from Liaoning District Postal Workers Entering the Pass 162

The Circumstances Before and After the Blockade

Ba Lidi Shed Blood for the Public Good

A Glimpse of the Surnames of Traitors The Northeast Postal Service, after the Ministry of Communications ordered the blockade, the Postal Directorate-General has received reports on the handling of the closure in various postal districts, but has not yet released them for the sake of prudence. The postal workers in the Liaoning, Jilin, and Heilongjiang districts, as a result of negotiations with the local postal directors, were all promised to be issued passports. At the same time, members of the Liaoning District Postal Affairs Club also arrived in Tianjin one after another and established an office in Tianjin to take care of the resettlement of postal workers entering the pass. The office also made a detailed report to the National Postal Workers Union on the process of the Shenyang Bureau's transfer and the total number of postal workers entering the pass until now, which is recorded below:

The Liaoning Postal District received the order to blockade on July 24. Postal Director Ba Lidi printed and issued a bureau notice and announcement that evening (3 o'clock in the afternoon), announcing the blockade and ordering the completion of mail sealing and delivery that evening. All employees were to leave the post office, leaving only two gatekeepers to guard. All doors were sealed, and all personnel were issued one month's salary (July salary) and travel expenses (calculated at half of August salary) from the 23rd and ordered to report to the four locations of Pingjin, Shanghai, and Qingdao respectively. However, the blockade order was issued very urgently at the time, and employees who were unable to receive their salaries were to receive them at the postal director's residence after the 24th. As soon as the Puppet State heard the news, it ordered police detectives to

guard the post office and the homes of all employees. The alert employees left for the pass on the evening of the 24th without any danger. Those who did not leave after the 25th were unable to do so because their homes were surrounded by police detectives, and the police officers strictly ordered the landlords and neighbors to monitor them and prevent them from escaping. For a time, many were detained and dared not move rashly. Even under these circumstances, personnel planned to enter the pass by traveling day and night. Some detoured through Andong and Yingkou, while others entered the pass through the Shenyu section of the Beining Road. It is estimated that there are now six or seven postal workers, sixty-nine postal assistants, and five hundred and thirty laborers in Tianjin, totaling six hundred and sixty-six people. In addition to those who have arrived and are successively reporting to the Tianjin Bureau and temporarily assigned to work in the management bureau and branches, people continue to arrive every day. The inns around Tianjin East Station are already overcrowded, but a small number of people

sell themselves to the Puppet State, hoping to become

officials of a fallen country. It is impossible to blame these few cold-blooded people, as human beings are not all the same. The urgent task at hand is to resettle the employees entering the pass, especially the lower-level laborers, whose salaries are too low. They risked their lives to come, and their aspirations are commendable. They should be given relief and protection. These laborers escaped alone, and their clothes and luggage are mostly missing, which is very pitiful. The headquarters is responsible for planning the welfare and relief of colleagues and cannot shirk this responsibility. Therefore, Jin Shaochu was assigned to take charge of the reception in Tianjin in advance, and Pingfang was in charge of the reception by Zheng Tingjie, with the support of friendly associations in various places. Now, the

aftermath of the personnel entering the pass is complicated, and efforts are needed in all aspects. An emergency meeting of the Standing Committee has been convened to decide to set up offices in Pingjin, Shanghai, and Qingdao. Zheng Tingjie, Song Baixiang, and Zhang Siwen will be in charge of Beiping; Jin Shaotian, Wang Weisi (currently in Yuguan), Jiang Fengshan, Jin Zhiming, Jin Zelun, and Li Wenqi will be in charge of organizing the offices in Tianjin. Efforts have been made to contact colleagues in Qingdao, and it is planned to have Li Xiong, Xiao Guohua, and He Hongtao organize offices in Shanghai to implement the Liaoning Postal Affairs

Colleagues Club office. All matters related to the welfare of colleagues, according to this blockade, were very urgent. Although employees were subjected to Japanese surveillance, Postal Director

Ba Lidi, under duress and high pressure, organized the bureau's affairs, maintained the employees, and worked day and night, even injecting stimulants to maintain his energy. His responsible spirit is worthy of respect by the Chinese people. Deputy Postal Director Liu Yaoting, under the siege of the Japanese, was coerced and enticed but did not move. Since October, he has assisted the postal director in handling everything, sharing hardships and dangers. His contribution is also indispensable. The colleagues of the headquarters should inform the workers of the whole country of the hardships of the responsible officials and comfort them upon their return.

Traitors According to recent investigations, there is a translator,

a native of Guangdong Province, named Weng Jian, who serves as an inspector at the Shenyang Puppet Bureau with a monthly salary of 180 yuan. The dismissed postal workers Wang Xijin and Lu Shuyou have all served in the Puppet Bureau. In addition, postal worker Wang Wenxiang has sold himself as a traitor and serves as the director of the business office. The rest have not yet been investigated and will be reported after investigation. In addition, the personnel restriction guarantee has been cancelled, and the truth is currently under investigation. Sincerely submitted to the National Postal Workers Union, Ning Postal Affairs Colleagues Club Executive Committee.
