Municipal Health Bureau Notifies Citizens 164

Implementing Disinfection of Well Water and Creek Water, Do Not Misunderstand This summer, the weather is extremely hot, and cholera has occurred in the city, with a very fierce momentum. The Municipal Health Bureau, based on the experience gained from years of cholera prevention investigations, has found that this disease in this city initially occurs mostly in residents in areas where tap water has not yet arrived and rely solely on drinking well water and creek water. In order to thoroughly eliminate the cholera hazard, the bureau has specially organized 12 disinfection teams this year, all wearing uniforms and distributing disinfection medicines, and assigning them to various parts of the city to carry out well water and flood water disinfection work. Since its implementation, considerable results have been achieved. However, during the work, citizens still do not understand the truth, are suspicious and panic, and misunderstandings have occurred. It is now heard that the bureau has specially notified citizens to explain the importance of well water and creek water disinfection, that the disinfection medicines used are harmless, and that there is no harm to citizens. It is hoped that citizens will not misunderstand. The bureau's announcement and leaflet to citizens are recorded below:

Announcement The Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau announces: False announcement matters, this year, cholera has occurred in the city, and its momentum is very strong. This disease is mostly caused by drinking unclean well water or creek water. In order to prevent it, the bureau has recently dispatched staff wearing uniforms, carrying disinfection medicines, to disinfect all well water and creek water in the city. The disinfection medicines used are harmless and do not harm the health of citizens. This work of the bureau is entirely for the purpose of protecting public health and eliminating the harm to citizens.

All are to be fully informed, do not be suspicious, do not panic, and do not misunderstand.

Do not add obstruction is necessary, carefully announce this.

Leaflet Citizens This summer, cholera

epidemics have occurred in the city, and the momentum is very fierce. I believe everyone has heard about it. This disease is mostly transmitted by unclean drinks, so the first places where it occurs are always in places where there is no tap water. Because residents in places where there is no tap water all drink unclean well water and dirty creek water, they are most likely to contract this epidemic. In order to eliminate this germ and avoid harm to citizens, the bureau has recently dispatched staff wearing uniforms, carrying disinfection medicines, to disinfect all well water and creek water. The disinfection medicines used are harmless and do not harm the health of citizens. This work of the bureau is entirely for the purpose of eliminating harm to citizens and seeking peace. We hope that everyone will not be suspicious or fearful, so as to cause misunderstandings and add obstruction. If there is any obstruction, hindering the performance of official duties, the bureau will handle it according to law and will never forgive it. Everyone must pay attention and persuade each other to take care of it. This is of utmost importance. Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau initiates,

Harbor Quarantine Office Cholera Report 165

Eleventh Period Harbor Quarantine Office Director and Shanghai Cholera Prevention Temporary Office Director Wu Liande yesterday (10th) issued the eleventh cholera weekly report as follows: (1) Since the cholera epidemic in Shanghai this year, it has been the fifteenth week. The past weekend (ending August 6), there were 454 new cholera cases, a decrease of 50 cases from the previous week. A list is shown below:

Number of Cases Deaths

Shanghai City 147 9 Public Concession 257 including 6 foreigners 23 including 2 foreigners French Concession 50 including 5 foreigners 7 including 1 foreigner Total 454 including 11 foreigners 39 including 3 foreigners Previous Total 2570 including 42 foreigners 175 including 12 foreigners

Grand Total 3024 including 53 foreigners 214 including 15 foreigners In view of the above, the mortality rate of cholera in Shanghai to date is 7%. (2) It has been found that the cholera epidemic in Guangzhou, Shantou, and other South China ports seems to have been alleviated. Recently, a report from Guangzhou stated that only 12 cases were seen in ten weeks, a large decrease compared to the 203 cases reported in the first week of July. Now the epidemic has spread to Dalian, Niuzhuang, Harbin, and Yantai, but the discovery is

late, and the climate is cool, so it should not be too rampant. (3) It has been found that ships coming to and from Shanghai port still have cholera cases. The details are as follows: (A) The Canadian Empress ship arrived in Kobe on August 8 and found that the ship's cook had died of cholera. The ship was quarantined for five days. (B) The Changsha ship

found a tea room attendant with cholera while being repaired in Shanghai Shipyard on August 3. The patient was immediately sent to the epidemic hospital, and 94 crew members were given prevention injections. The entire ship was disinfected. (C) The Japanese Deng ship Nagasaki Maru left Shanghai on August 4. Due to suspected cholera patients being found on board, the ship was ordered to stay in the port for 14 hours when it arrived in Nagasaki the next day before being allowed to proceed to Kobe. (4) The Ministry of Interior's Health Department announced that this year's cholera epidemic has spread to almost the entire country, with epidemics reaching 15 provinces, including coastal ports, involving 120 counties. It can be said to be extremely rampant. Fortunately, peacetime defenses were properly implemented, and many prevention injection vaccines were prepared, so it was not too difficult to handle. (5) It has been found that this year's cholera prevention relies on the cooperation of all sectors, and the effectiveness is not small, especially the effectiveness of prevention injections. The number of injections is currently being statistically analyzed, because some citizens voluntarily invited doctors or went directly to the hospital to request injections, and some voluntarily paid high consultation fees to seek prevention injections. It can be seen that the public has a considerable understanding of injections. Some people may ask what is the effectiveness of using oral medicines to prevent cholera. It is undoubtedly more effective to use oral prevention medicines to prevent typhoid fever, but there is no significant record for preventing cholera. As for the method of subcutaneous injection prevention, according to experience, it is indeed effective in preventing infection. According to the experience gained, two injections are given every other week, and the immune effect can last for six months. However, the vaccine made in this country is more effective than the imported one, because the germicidal effect of the imported vaccine is weakened for people in this country. But regardless of whether or not injections are given, it is most important to avoid eating raw and cold foods and using unclean water. (6) Now, one case of someone who received one injection and still contracted cholera is briefly described as follows: Zhang, a rat catcher at this office, 34 years old, recently contracted mild cholera (confirmed by bacterial test). He was sent to the Shanghai Epidemic Hospital on Xizang Road on August 4 and was cured after receiving salt water injection treatment. It was found that this person had only received one injection three months ago.

Fisheries Administration Bureau 172

Reorganization Completed Under Orders 173

Ten District Offices Established Yesterday

and Actively Preparing to Establish the Fisheries Bank of the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Fisheries Administration Bureau, since it was ordered to reorganize last month and changed its name, the director of the bureau, Fan Zhilong, in order to develop fisheries and expand police force, specially purchased patrol ships and supplemented the number of police officers. The bureau was also officially established a few days ago. At the same time, the branch offices were also established yesterday. The details are recorded as follows:

Expanding the Original Police Force The bureau was ordered to reorganize by the Executive Yuan, and after being passed by the Legislative Yuan, it immediately followed the new organizational law to carry out reorganization, and was renamed (Jiangsu-Zhejiang District Marine Fisheries Administration Bureau). In view of the recent rampant piracy, the bureau's police force was weak, so in addition to the original four patrol ships, it also converted the Jinghai and Xinglong merchant ships into patrol ships a few days ago. In addition, a number of small steamships were purchased) for patrol use. The original fishing protection team was expanded into a large team, divided into five detachments, stationed in various parts of Nantong, to protect fishermen, and a large number of military supplies were purchased, so the police force after the reorganization was quite strong.

Establishing Branch Offices The bureau should establish branch offices in various coastal areas in accordance with the organizational law in order to protect the fishermen nearby. Now Director Fan has stipulated that the two provinces of Jiangsu and Zhejiang are divided into ten districts, including three in Jiangsu: Songhu, Tongzhou, and Haizhou; and seven in Zhejiang: Haining, Dinghai, Zhenhai, Wenzhou, Zhapu, Xiangshan, and Taizhou. The candidates for the directors of each district have been appointed by Fan and filed with the Ministry of Industry and Commerce. Currently, the personnel have gone to their respective posts.

Names of District Directors The names of the directors of each district are recorded as follows: Haining Hua Zhiheng, Dinghai Tao Mengzhao, Zhenhai Xu Zhenxu, Wenzhou Hang Shiwei, Zhapu Tong Zhiyi, Xiangshan Chen Zheng, Taizhou Liang Zhaohong, Songhu An Qi, Tongzhou Liang Qixian, Haizhou Zhu Shiqing,

Collecting Special Fishing Protection Fees After the establishment of the branch offices, special protection fees will be collected in accordance with the organizational law. The method is that in addition to (the bureau being responsible for protecting fishing boats as usual), if fishermen request the bureau to specially dispatch fishing protection teams or patrol ships for protection, the requested fishing boats will be charged a special protection fee according to the size of the boat and the distance of the route. However, the number is more during the spring and autumn fishing seasons each year, and very few at ordinary times.

Organizing a Fisheries Bank In order to develop the future of the marine industry, the bureau has specially planned to set up a fisheries bank. According to Secretary Sun of the bureau speaking to the Huadong News Agency reporter, the bank plans to have a share capital of 5 million yuan, and is of a limited nature. In order to popularize the share capital, all fishing firms will be shareholders, and the bureau will also add official shares depending on the economic strength, so that it can proceed. All plans have been formulated and will be carried out soon.

Martial Arts Novels Harm People 177

Elementary School Student Goes Missing 178

A suicide note says he went to the Western Paradise

No abnormalities were seen when he came to Shanghai from Yangzhou

After arriving in Shanghai, he was reported missing again

The family is anxiously waiting to die Since the popularity of martial arts novels, many minors have been confused by them. Recently, Zhang Zhaishou of Shengping Lane, Taifu Street, Yangzhou, has a son named Zhang Zhishun, who is only thirteen years old. He is usually obsessed with martial arts novels. On the morning of the twelfth of last month, he went to school from home and never returned. The family did not see him return home for lunch and was very surprised. They went to the school to inquire, but he did not go to school. They searched everywhere, but there was no trace. Later, a note was found on the desk at home, which read (I went to the Western Paradise with the holy monk, don't miss me). The handwriting was indeed Zhishun's own. Knowing that he had traveled far, the whole family was worried and didn't know what to do. His parents were especially anxious and wanted to die. After leaving home, Zhishun came to Shanghai alone on the thirteenth and turned to his uncle and sister, claiming that he came with his classmates. When asked about the names and addresses of his classmates, he was evasive, and he did not bring any change of clothes. His uncle and sister were very surprised, but because his mother had said in Shanghai last year that Zhishun wanted to come but did not succeed, now seeing him come alone, they thought it was a fulfillment of his long-cherished wish, and at most they only suspected that the child was greedy and playful and came to Shanghai privately. After he came, his goal had been achieved, and there would be no more accidents. The next day, they sent a letter to Yangzhou to inquire, but before the reply came, Zhishun disappeared again. Before that, after Zhishun came to Shanghai, he was very happy with his younger brother, sister, and nephews, and became friends with children of similar ages in the same neighborhood at first sight. All day long, besides playing with his companions or telling stories, he never put down the books in his hands. When he read what books, they were all martial arts swordsmen, such as those for several days, without any abnormalities. Unexpectedly, after lunch on the 20th, he suddenly disappeared. At first, he thought he was playing with his companions at the home of a neighbor in the same neighborhood. By 4:00 PM, he was looking for snacks but could not find him. He asked the children of the families he played with, and they all said they had not seen him. Only then did he realize that something was wrong. He checked the boxes and found that 10 yuan in banknotes and 1.2 yuan in savings left over from his arrival were missing. He immediately sent someone to the west to search and went to the station to look for him, but there was no trace. One day after he ran away from his Shanghai residence, he received a letter from his family explaining the past situation and firmly urging him not to let him go. How could he know that the letter had not arrived and the person had left? But he still hoped that the one who went out suddenly would drift back. He sent a letter to Yangzhou to inquire, and then received a letter saying that he had not returned. Until now, this poor child is still the target of daily anticipation of his relatives in Shanghai and Yangzhou, and he has no money left. Where has he been relying on for more than ten days? It is really puzzling. If any charitable organizations, monasteries, and people from all walks of life know of his whereabouts and report them to his family, it would be a great merit. (Mailing address: Ruan Jingru, Shanghai Sanma Road Xinwen Newspaper Office)

A Woman's Life of Misery 179

Ends in Suicide 180

Alas, Poverty, the Eldest Son Commits Suicide

The Landlord Forces Relocation, and She Hangs Herself in the Middle of the Night Mrs. Lu Xi, 51 years old, hanged herself at home at 3:00 AM yesterday due to economic pressure. The police have been notified for inspection and burial. The tragic history of her family is recorded below.

The Family History of the Deceased Lu Xi, from Changshu, lived at No. 12, Huayuan Stone Bridge, Pudong. Her husband died more than 20 years ago, leaving behind one son (named Mingzhong) and two daughters, who were still in swaddling clothes. The pillar of Xi's family was suddenly broken, and her livelihood was cut off. She hurriedly coffined and buried her husband, and worked hard to try to maintain for several years. The difficulties during this period need not be said. Later, relatives and friends saw her and pitied her, so they introduced a fellow villager named Xiangbao to fill the room as her husband. Xi's mother and son and three others were able to have someone to take care of them and would not be reduced to starving to death. This was more than ten years ago.

The Suicide of the Eldest Son Later, Mingzhong grew up and was introduced to work as a driver at the Nanyang Printing House on Tao Peng Road in Hudong. He also married and had children. In the year before last (19th year), Mingzhong was 25 years old. His stepfather was old and unable to produce, so the five members of the family depended on Mingzhong alone to make a living. Mingzhong had limited income and huge household expenses. He also borrowed more than 100 yuan from the landlord Gu Longlong, which he could not repay. He committed suicide by swallowing sleeping pills at 10:00 PM on May 16 of this year. When his family found out, he had already died of poisoning and could not be saved. His situation was reported in various newspapers the next day. Later, two suicide notes were found in his bedroom, one to his mother and one to his cousin. Reading his letter to his mother, every word was a tear, and he couldn't bear to finish reading it. Excerpts from a few words are quoted below, (The man has been living in the city of sorrow every day in the past two weeks. He is so poor now, his debts are piling up, his clothes are all gone, he has no way to borrow money, he can't eat enough, he can't wear warm clothes, and the family expenses are very large. The wages earned by the man are not enough for household use. This is entirely the man's fault. He has not repaid the kindness of raising him, and he often sees adults shedding tears. The man's heart aches so much. The father's coffin has been in Chang for more than 20 years and has not been buried. This is also the man's fault. The man has grown up to 25 years old and cannot support the adults and the whole family. He is really ashamed and standing in the world, so he has to take this dead end. Your daughter-in-law is very young. Nowadays, few women observe chastity. If he is righteous, he will live a good life with his family. If he is not righteous, let her be. Only the granddaughter must not be taken away by others. Please ask the adults to take her to the infant hall.)

Hanging Herself Due to Relocation After Mingzhong's death, Xi's eldest daughter went to the Nanyang Cigarette Factory to pick out tobacco silk, and the second daughter went to the Tianzhang Paper Factory to pick out old cloth. She earned a few corners of silver every day to maintain the family's livelihood, but she was often insufficient. She accumulated more than one year's rent (three and a half yuan per month). During the year, she only paid 37 yuan of rent. The landlord urged her to pay urgently. If she could not cope, she would have to move out. Xi found a flat house in Gu Sanshan, paid a deposit of three yuan, and declared to the old landlord Gu Longlong that she would move out by the tenth of this month (ie, yesterday). Gu Sanshan suddenly returned the deposit, so the lease was not completed. By 3:00 AM yesterday, Xi was forced to hang herself because the deadline for relocation had arrived and she saw that there was nowhere to move. At that time, her family was still asleep. When they found out at dawn, she had already died and her body was cold. Xi's stepfather Xiangbao accused the landlord Gu Longlong of forcing her to death to the Third District. The district ordered Gu to be summoned to the case for questioning, and then he was temporarily released on bail.

Funeral Arrangements The Third District Public Security Bureau issued a notice to the local security officer Xie Along yesterday morning, requesting the local court to send someone to examine the body. In the afternoon, Prosecutor Yang and Inspector Shen arrived at the scene for examination. It was found that Xi had committed suicide by hanging. He ordered the family to prepare a coffin for burial first, while the corpse's daughter-in-law Hu and the corpse's daughters knelt in front of the coffin and shouted for injustice. The official ordered them to file a lawsuit according to the law. It is reported that the Pudong Fifth District Cigarette, Loading and Unloading, Paper Making, Cotton Weaving, and Japan-China Branch Offices and other groups have raised funds because the coffin and burial expenses of the deceased were not available, and have jointly submitted a public request to the party and government agencies for assistance.

The First Special Court Hears 181

The Case of the Brutal Murder of a Mistress 182

Pu Henian Talks Eloquently

Narrates the Process of the Murder Without Reservation Pu Henian (23 years old), a native of Qingpu, lived in the back building of the Yun Ji Zhang Xiaoquan Scissors Shop at No. 825, Dongxi Huade Road. At noon the day before yesterday, he killed his mistress Wang Xiuying with a kitchen knife due to jealousy and hatred. The Huishan Patrol Room received a report and sent detectives to arrest the murderer Pu Henian. The deceased was carried into the morgue. Yesterday morning, he was escorted to the Fourth Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. Zhang Tianyin, a lawyer from the patrol room, stated the case and presented the murder weapon and a photo of the deceased and the defendant together for inspection. He continued that the blood stains on the knife were obvious, and there was a strand of hair stuck to it, which was unbearable to see. When questioned, the defendant Pu Henian confessed that he used to be in the cotton business and is now selling Rendan. The deceased Wang Xiuying was 25 years old and from Suzhou. On March 24 of this year, I took a boat to Shanghai from Suzhou. I met her on the boat and talked to each other. She asked me where I was going. I replied that I was going to Shanghai to do a small business. She said that she was also going to Shanghai to visit relatives, so we were intimate with each other. After arriving in Shanghai, we went to the Kaiji Sheng Inn on Fuzhou Road for one night. The next day, we went to the Donghai Hotel on Houma Road and stayed for more than two months. Because the expenses were not enough, we moved to a kitchen shed rented in Shangyi Lane, Baxianqiao, in the French Concession. We lived there for a month. This was known to my fiancee Shunbao from my hometown, who came to make trouble. Wang Xiuying told me to abandon her, so I avoided her and stayed at the Yingbin Hotel for two nights. My wife could not return home and was afraid of causing trouble again, so we moved to the back building of No. 825, Dongxi Huade Road. Recently, due to economic difficulties, I sold Rendan on various roads, earning a few corners every day, but it was still not enough for expenses, and Wang Xiuying often went out and behaved irregularly. Four days ago, she did not return one night. The next day, when I asked her, she claimed to be staying with her little sisters. Unexpectedly, the night before last, she did not return again until 11:00 the next day. When I asked her slightly, I was greatly scolded, saying that I should make a voucher to sever all ties forever. If I don't measure my strength, I will give you some color, and said that I would cut it in half with one knife and find my own way. When I heard this, I was so angry that I couldn't restrain myself. I recalled that I was a young man, and I regretted being blind and being deceived by her. Now that the money is gone, she wants me to break up. Although I was fooled, I have already made a mistake, and it is too late to regret. Therefore, I could not vent my anger. I took a kitchen knife from behind the door and killed her, and did not try to escape. I planned to call the patrol, but the second landlord Liu Cao Shi arrived and twisted me up. Liu Cao Shi testified that the defendant moved in for only more than 20 days. At that time, he claimed to be a teacher in a school, and there were only two of them, husband and wife. They were usually harmonious, and no relatives or friends came. A few days ago, Wang Xiuying did not return one night, and it was not heard that there was any conflict with the defendant. The night before last, she did not go home again until noon the next day. Then I heard a quarrel. I ordered the apprentice to inquire, and he replied that nothing happened. Suddenly, I heard a cry for help, so I went upstairs to persuade her. I saw that the door was closed. Peeking through the cracks, Wang Xiuying was covered in blood and rolling around on the ground. I was so shocked that I ran downstairs and called the police. The defendant was already walking down the escalator and was twisted and handed over to the police for detention. Feng Yonglin, who lived on the front building of the house, testified that he went out to see a doctor because he was sick. When he came back, he saw the back building calling for help and knocked on the door but it did not open. After a while, the second landlord and the police arrived and arrested the defendant. After Shen Bingrong, the judge, verified the confession, he said that the facts of the case were very clear and ordered the defendant to be sent to the morgue for questioning. At 11:00, Zhan Liangce, the prosecutor appointed by the Special Court, arrived at the office and verified that the woman Wang Xiuying had been stabbed to death with a sharp weapon while she was alive. The murderer Pu Henian was taken into custody for investigation, and the corpse was handed over to the Pushan Villa for coffining and burial.

Continued Report on the Nightingale Case 183

Bathroom Inn Tea Server Appears in Court to Testify

Fan Hongsheng Suffered from a Nervous Disorder

Once Hospitalized, He Bit Through Iron Chains and Escaped

This case is adjourned for one week for further hearing. Nanjing native Fan Hongsheng (i.e., Fan Ruibao) went to the residence of female fortune teller Wang Wenyin at No. 89 Pingle Lane, Xizang Road, at 3:05 PM on July 19 of this year, fatally stabbed Wang, and Wang's mother, Wu, was also injured in the attack. Fan fled the scene and disappeared without a trace. Subsequently, after a thorough investigation by Chinese Detective Yu A'gen, Su Changsheng, Detective Zhou Guisheng, Zhao Ziren of the Old Gate Police Station, it was discovered that Fan was hiding at his sister's residence at No. 965 Jiaotong Road, Zhabei, and he was arrested. Jun'ao Ke Cheng Meixian, Wang Wenyin's teacher, was also suspected of involvement and arrested. After investigation, it was found that Cheng was not involved, and the court was requested to order his release on bail. Fan was then sent to the First Special Court for interrogation. Fan's lawyer, Jiang Baoli, argued that Fan suffered from a mental disorder and should be exempt from criminal punishment according to the law, requesting an adjournment to present evidence proving his condition. The court granted the request and announced a postponement. The details have been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday morning, the hearing resumed. Presiding Judge Feng Shide of the Criminal Court resumed the hearing in the Second Criminal Court. First, the police lawyer, Ru Baoyi, stated that the court had previously ordered investigations into the Longquan Bathhouse and the Yadong Hotel, which had now been completed, as reported by the detectives. Detective Su then testified, "I went to Longquan for investigation. They replied that the defendant had been to the bathhouse between 1:00 and 2:00 PM on the day of the incident and left shortly after." Detective Zhou then testified, "My investigation confirmed that the defendant and Wenyin lived together in a room at the Yadong Hotel." He then submitted the registration book as evidence. Lin A'er, a tea server at the Yadong Hotel, testified that Fan Hongsheng and Wenyin came to rent Room 11 in May, stayed for two days, and then came again in early June for three days. Li Hongsheng, a tea server at the Longquan Bathhouse, also testified, stating that Fan came on July 19 before 1:00 PM, stayed for about fifteen minutes, and then left. He also stated that Fan came to bathe from time to time, and whenever he saw people talking, he would suspect they were scolding him, indiscriminately scolding anyone, whether familiar or not. Even I was sometimes subjected to his insults and scolding. I knew he had a mental illness, so I didn't argue with him." At this point, the defendant's lawyer, Jiang Baoli, stated, "Now I have two pieces of physical evidence and three witnesses, all of which are sufficient to prove that the defendant does indeed have a mental illness. The physical evidence consists of reply letters from Xin Puyu Hall and Suzhou Gospel Hospital to our law firm. The witnesses are the defendant's landlord, his mother, and his brother." According to the letter from Xin Puyu Hall, on August 7 of last year, while the defendant was being treated for madness at the hall, he bit through extremely strong iron chains and escaped by jumping off the roof. This happened twice. The letter from Gospel Hospital stated that the defendant was discharged on January 6 and would have needed to stay for another year to fully recover, which proves that his illness was not cured. This is clear evidence." He then submitted the two letters as evidence and stated, "After the January 28th Incident, the defendant gave everyone who worked with him at the former Railway Bureau business cards with titles such as 'Communist Party Member, Shanghai'... but all of them were unable to come to court to testify due to their positions. Moreover, his old illness relapsed again around May 27. All of this is sufficient to prove the defendant's mental incapacity beyond any doubt." The witness Luo Linmei, a woman of 23 years of age from Shaoxing, residing at No. 1329 Wenjian Shi Road, testified, "The defendant's sister lives with me, and Fan often comes to my sister's house. When Fan goes crazy, he throws things on the ground and yells at people. Sometimes he even catches flies and eats them. When my family lit incense on the first and fifteenth of the lunar month, he burned his hand with the candle and sat on top of the car instead of inside it. Therefore, the residents of Wenjian Shi Road all regard him as a madman. He seemed to have recovered slightly after leaving the hospital this year, but unexpectedly, his old illness relapsed around May 20-something. My mother couldn't stand the fright, so she told Fan's sister to move out, which they did in early June. I don't know what happened after that." Fan's brother, Fan Hongbin, who works at the Railway Bureau as the station master of Nanjing Station, testified, "Hong Sheng's madness was entirely due to the excessive stimulation he suffered from the divorce lawsuit with his wife, Xiuying. Hong Sheng told me that Xiuying (who was also in court listening, wearing a red floral qipao and a corsage, her face covered in rouge) had been unfaithful even before they married, but he still cared for her very much. However, Xiuying suddenly returned to Ning that year, which led to the lawsuit. As a result, Hong Sheng and Xiuying had two fights, which were taken to the police station and the police department. On July 6 of this year, Hong Sheng came to Nanjing and asked me for fifteen yuan for injections. He also said to me, 'You sent me to the hospital, and the doctor injected me with syphilis. You must be careful, I will kill you and your wife.' I gave him three yuan and sent someone to escort him to Shanghai, and explained the situation at Xin Puyu Hall, etc." Fan's mother, Li, also testified that Fan Hongsheng recently tried to cut out his heart with a knife and grabbed her hand, pulling her to dance. When questioned, Fan Hongsheng denied having a mental disorder. Lawyer Jiang then stated that people with mental illness never admit it and deeply resent others saying they are sick. Police Lawyer Ru, because the cause of the defendant's crime in this case is still difficult to prove, requested the court to postpone the hearing for another week for investigation. The court granted the request and adjourned.

National Federation of Commerce Urges 189

Provincial Federations of Commerce to Reorganize Promptly 190

The National Federation of Commerce yesterday telegraphed the Guangdong, Fujian, Jiangxi, Sichuan, Yunnan, Shanxi, Gansu, Rehe, Chahar, Guangxi, Guizhou, and Xinjiang Provincial Federations of Commerce, stating: "It is found that as of now, there are still thirteen provinces, including your federation, that have not been reorganized according to law. Our federation has previously telegraphed repeatedly to urge you, but you have not been able to complete it within the time limit. Moreover, Article 37, paragraph 2 of the Commercial Association Law stipulates that the establishment of the Commercial Association of the Republic of China shall require more than one-fourth of the provincial commercial associations and special municipal commercial associations as initiators and the consent of more than two-thirds of the provincial commercial associations and special municipal commercial associations to formulate articles of association and submit them to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce (now the Ministry of Industry) for approval and report to the National Government for record. Currently, all the provincial commercial associations and special municipal commercial associations that have been reorganized according to law do not meet the legal number, so our federation has not been able to reorganize according to law. Therefore, your federation's failure to reorganize is hindering our federation's progress. Accordingly, we are telegraphing again for your federation to investigate and immediately urge all commercial associations to reorganize and schedule a reorganization of the provincial federation of commerce. Please report the progress to the federation at any time. Sincerely hope. Chairman of the National Federation of Commerce, Lin Kanghou."

Recent News on the San You Labor-Management Dispute 191

The Cotton Weaving Industry Union of the Seventh District of Shanghai has prepared a document to submit to the Municipal Party Department and the Social Bureau regarding the San You Factory dispute, reporting that the management is deliberately making things difficult and reducing food expenses, leading to agitation among the public, which is impossible to stop. The shutdown since the January 28th Shanghai War has not yet been resolved. The affiliated associations have repeatedly submitted reports to the municipal government and your bureau regarding the situation. The municipal government issued Directive No. 142, ordering the management to be responsible for providing food for the workers before the case is resolved according to law. However, the management still wants to resist stubbornly. Fortunately, your bureau strictly ordered the management to provide a daily food allowance of 120 yuan to temporarily maintain two meals a day and barely make a living. The management not only does not show compassion but also relapses into its old habits, stubbornly going its own way, arbitrarily making things difficult, and recently reducing the food allowance to 100 yuan per day. How can this meager amount maintain the lives of more than a thousand people (according to the most recent re-registration)? The people are indignant and cannot express it. The responsible personnel of the affiliated associations are unable to maintain the situation under these circumstances. Therefore, a special document is submitted to request prompt and proper measures to calm the public's anger. Respectfully submitted to the Shanghai Social Bureau, Shanghai Cotton Weaving Industry Union of the Seventh District.

Resolution of Minor Dispute at Minsheng Rubber Factory 192

Social Bureau's Mediation Results

On the 24th of last month, Zhu Haisong, a supervisory staff member of the Minsheng Rubber Factory on Lujiabang Road in Nanshi, had a verbal argument with female worker Chen Caixian over a minor matter, which escalated into physical violence, injuring Caixian's left wrist. The male and female workers nearby were indignant and sparked a minor dispute. A reporter from the newspaper learned yesterday that the dispute had been handed over to the Social Bureau for handling. Yesterday morning at 9:00 AM, both parties went to the bureau, where Peng Zhenqiu of the Third Section convened them in the bureau's First Mediation Room to conduct mediation. As a result, it was decided that Zhu Haisong would compensate Chen Caixian for medical expenses and lost wages totaling 12.5 yuan. Both parties signed an agreement, and the matter was resolved. The record of the settlement is transcribed below: Labor side: female worker Chen Caixian; Management side: Zhu Haisong, staff member of Minsheng Rubber Factory. Regarding the dispute over the staff member's beating of the female worker, the bureau convened a mediation, and the parties have agreed to a settlement. A record is made as follows: (1) Zhu Haisong will pay Chen Caixian 9 yuan for medical expenses; (2) Chen Caixian was unable to work for seven days due to the injury, and Zhu Haisong will compensate 0.5 yuan per day for lost wages.

Shanghai Municipal Council Lawyer's Work Report for July 196

The Shanghai Municipal Council lawyer's report for July states that during July, a total of 10,646 cases were filed in the First District Court and the Second Branch of the High Court, including 8,335 minor cases in which the defendants did not appear and the bail was confiscated. A total of 2,250 cases were completed, in which 2,092 people were found guilty and sentenced, and 158 people were acquitted. Regarding appeals, the Municipal Council filed 7 cases, and the defendants filed 51 cases. Of the 46 defendant appeals that were concluded, 5 were acquitted, 23 appeals were rejected, 1 appeal was withdrawn, 3 were remanded for retrial, 1 sentence was increased, and 13 sentences were reduced. In addition, the Municipal Council requested 67 remands, resulting in 72 new indictments. As of the end of the month, there were 47 first-instance cases and 121 appeals pending in the two courts, for a total of 168 pending cases. There were 44 cases of probation this month. There were 16 cases of requests for extradition from outside the settlement, involving 24 people. Preliminary evidence was found in 10 cases, involving 15 offenders, who have been handed over. In 2 cases, 2 people were released on bail, and 1 person was acquitted. In addition, 2 murder suspects requested for extradition from Hong Kong were tried in Shanghai because the local court claimed jurisdiction. There are also 4 people in remand. Including the 7 people in remand since June, the agencies requesting the extradition have already been handed over. There were 14 stamp tax cases this month, in which 2 were withdrawn, and the rest were fined from 10 to 30 yuan. There were 12 cigarette tax cases, in which 10 were found guilty, and 2 were remanded, with 2 pending. During this month, 6,151 criminal summonses were handled by the patrol police, and 310 were handled by the judicial police. There were 7,271 civil summonses. There were 27 prisoners released this month in accordance with the amnesty decree.

Results of the Overseas Chinese Cup Shooting Competition 198

Unprecedented achievement by Singaporean Overseas Chinese. The Overseas Chinese Cup, donated by Mr. Ge Leilie, former captain of the Chinese team of the Shanghai International Merchant Corps, specifically for the shooting competition between Chinese merchant corps in various ports in the Far East, was again used for this year's remote competition between Shanghai and Singapore last month. The shooting results of the Shanghai team have been reported in the previous newspaper. It is now reported that the Singapore competition was held on the 24th of last month.

Page 16

The list of results was sent to Shanghai the day before yesterday. The total score was 850 points, exceeding Shanghai's 808 points by 42 points, breaking the highest record, which is rare in the past. It has been nine years since Shanghai and Singapore competed for this cup, and Shanghai has continuously maintained the championship for seven years. Even in this competition, Shanghai scored a total of 808 points, which is a great improvement over last year's 795 points. It was not easy.

###

However, the news came that Singapore has made great strides and achieved this amazing result, winning the championship for the second time. This shows the rapid progress of the shooting skills of our Chinese people, and it is especially commendable that Singaporean Chinese merchants have persevered and not slackened due to repeated defeats. It is now reported that the Shanghai Chinese team has sent a letter to congratulate them on their success and will declare the cup for shipment to Singapore. The cup is two feet tall and exquisitely carved. A reduced-size image is specially made above.

The District Court Burned Opium Yesterday 199

The opium, opium paste, morphine, heroin, red pills, and paraphernalia confiscated in all opium cases from July 1st of last year to the end of the year, totaling 4,948 items, were burned yesterday morning in the courtyard of the court. Those who went to the site to supervise included Tang Zaili, representative of the Ministry of Judicial Administration; Zhu Zongjian of the Higher Court; Li Yudong of the Garrison Headquarters; Wang Zongjian of the Jianghai Customs Superintendent's Office; Zhang Wenyu of the Second Special District Court; Ren Bin of the Municipal Party Department; Wang Yiqian of the Public Security Bureau; Zhang Zhentan of the Anti-Drug Association; as well as Shen Xiqing, President of the Court, and Liu Maochu, Chief Prosecutor. The burning started at 9:00 AM and continued until 6:00 PM. A total of 7,607 taels and 8 qian of opium, 442 taels, 2 qian, and 1 fen of opium paste, 19 taels, 1 qian, and 9 fen of opium dross, 21 taels, 6 qian, and 1 fen of opium bubbles, also 279 pieces, 124 taels and 5 qian, also 20 small packages, 10 jin of pill material, 3 small bottles of medicinal powder, 90 taels, 0 qian, and 8 fen of morphine, 2 fen of heroin, and 3,533 taels, 8 qian, also 106 jin of red pills were burned.

Three Female Corpses Recovered Again Yesterday from the Japanese Ship Collision with a Sampan 200

The Japanese ship Hakone Maru collided with a sampan the day before yesterday, causing more than ten female passengers to fall into the water. Only one woman was rescued. After the accident, two drowned corpses were recovered by fishing boats, and the rest were missing. The details were reported in yesterday's newspaper. According to the news from the Water Patrol Police Station yesterday, the sampan has been detained, and the two boatmen, Du Jutian and Du Xiaodingzi, have also been sent to the Nanshi District Court Prosecutor's Office. In addition to the two bodies recovered the day before yesterday, three more bodies were recovered by fishing boats yesterday, all female corpses. When they were recovered, the families of the deceased were on the shore, unwilling to have them inspected, and they were immediately taken away for burial. Therefore, the police station has not been able to ascertain the names and ages of the deceased and is currently ordering detectives to investigate for reference.

Amicable Settlement Expected in the Case of Wu Jiangguang's Son Accused of Seduction 201

Shen Ai'e, a female employee of the ABC Commercial Printing House on Jiujiang Road, recently filed a lawsuit in the First Special District Court against Wu Zhongliang, the son of the blind Wu Jiangguang, for seduction, etc., with her mother, Shen Chu, and hired lawyer Xue Jiaqi. The court has interrogated the parties three times. The details have been repeatedly reported in this newspaper. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Wu Tingqi resumed the hearing in the Second Criminal Court. Both the plaintiff and the defendant appeared in court. The defendant's agent, lawyer Zheng Wenkai, stated that the case is currently being mediated by relatives and friends of both parties, so there is a strong hope of settlement. He requested a postponement for further hearing, and the plaintiff's agent, lawyer Xue, also agreed. Judge Wu then announced that the case would be postponed for seven days for further hearing.

Old Tenants Sue for Renewal of Leases on New Houses 202

More than thirty municipal houses in front of the Jinting Guild Hall on Lujiabang Road, Daxing Street, Xiaoximen, are properties of the guild hall. Recently, due to the renovation of new houses, the regular tenants believed that the standing directors of the guild hall, Xu Huimin, etc., did not notify the tenants, which clearly had other intentions. Therefore, the tenants elected Dan Yunsheng, etc., as representatives and hired lawyer Jin Hongji to apply to the mediation office of the district court for mediation for lease renewal to alleviate business difficulties. Since mediation failed, Dan Yunsheng, etc., formally filed a lawsuit.

Anlegong's Violation of Regulations and Fines 203

Japanese dancers failed to comply with the regulations to get vaccinations. The Anlegong Dance Hall at No. 57-59 Avenue Edward VII in the French Concession was recently summoned to the Second Criminal Court of the Second Special District Court by the police station for violating Article 3 of the Municipal Council's regulations on employing female servants in public entertainment venues. First, police lawyer Yuan Jiahong stated the case, saying that the defendant had been found to have violated the time regulations a week ago and was fined 100 yuan by the court. A month ago, the Municipal Council's Health Department sent someone to inform that all female employees and dancers in the venue must be vaccinated and inoculated with cowpox at the Municipal Council, and certificates should be presented when inspected by Municipal Council officials. However, it is now found that the defendant's venue ignored this and still did not send the dancers for vaccinations at the Municipal Council, which is a violation of the above regulations and should be punished. The defendant, Chen Zhanxiong, who was represented by Yan Bingxian, stated that there are more than fifty dancers in the venue, most of whom are Japanese women. More than ten of them have already been vaccinated by doctors and have certificates to prove it. He also hired a lawyer to defend him. An overseas employee of the Health Department then stated that the department had sent people to inform three times. The vaccination certificates of the Japanese dancers presented by the defendant were not from doctors who had registered with the department and could not be considered valid. After verifying the供 by Judge Zhang Chaozuo, he announced the end of the debate and immediately sentenced the defendant Chen Zhanxiong to a fine of 80 yuan for violating the regulations.

Wu Yousheng Disappears While Collecting Debts 204

Debtor Claims Not to Have Seen Him for Many Days

Family Suspects Foul Play. Wu Yousheng, a Ningbo native, 51 years old, residing at No. 18 Baoyu Lane, Caishi Street, French Concession, is currently engaged in the auction business, negotiating transactions at the Yiyuan Tea House on Wuma Road every day. He is quite honest and trusted by his colleagues. His business has been good in recent years. Although he has no large savings, he often has dealings with money shops. On the morning of the day before yesterday (the 8th), he left home at 9:00 AM, carrying a money shop draft for more than 100 taels, intending to collect a debt of 240 taels from Shi A'ru, a current milk powder broker, in the Hekang Lane in the city's Nine Mu Di. He did not return that night and was reported missing. His family was extremely anxious and went to Shi's place to inquire, but Shi claimed that he had not seen Yousheng for more than a month and had not come, nor did he owe him any money. The family, upon hearing this, thought it suspicious because Yousheng had played mahjong with A'ru at the home of Shi's friend, someone Jia, the day before. Now he suddenly claimed that he had not seen him for more than a month and did not admit to owing him money, which clearly indicated other circumstances. In addition to reporting the matter to the British and French police stations for investigation, the family also submitted a report to the Municipal Public Security Bureau yesterday requesting an investigation. Wu was wearing a black Xiangyunsha short shirt and pants and a copper pot hat when he disappeared. He has been missing for two days.

Du Yuesheng Founds Gaohang Epidemic Hospital, Begins Treatment 207

Due to the severe epidemic near Gaohang Town in Pudong, local people requested Mr. Du Yuesheng to donate funds to establish an epidemic hospital and treat various prevalent diseases. Recent News from the Jiyi Benevolent Society Epidemic Hospital 208

The Jiyi Benevolent Society in this city has been operating the epidemic hospital it established on Tangshan Road in Hongkou for nearly two months. The epidemic prevention work has never been relaxed. In total, the outpatient department has seen approximately 20,000 patients. Although the heat has recently subsided, the hospital still has around 400 patients every day, and many are critically ill. Therefore, although the equipment is sufficient, the wards are still overcrowded. This is because most of the residents in Hongkou are poor households who rarely pay attention to hygiene. The proliferation of factories, polluted air, and unclean food are all causes of disease. The hospital sees that the autumn epidemic is on the rise, and epidemic prevention work cannot be delayed. Therefore, it has expanded its premises to avoid the poor and sick from having to travel in vain. Moreover, the medical directors Lin Chunshan and Zhu Xiaofang have extensive experience with epidemics and do not spare any effort, working tirelessly day and night. All the staff members are also selfless and work together to ensure the safety of the epidemic victims. Therefore, although its history is short, its reputation has spread throughout Shanghai. People from afar come to seek treatment, and donations are made daily. The touching depth of their work can be seen from this. According to the hospital authorities, the autumn epidemic is originally easier to spread than the summer epidemic. In addition, most Chinese civilians lack common hygiene knowledge and do not regulate their daily lives, eating, and drinking habits. When they are sick, they do not seek medical treatment quickly, or they pray to gods and Buddhas or scrape away "sha." By the time they are sent to the hospital when they are critically ill, they cannot follow the hospital's regulations and often secretly bring food to patients, causing repeated complications and making treatment impossible. They greedily indulge in momentary pleasure, and in a blink of an eye, they will lose their lives without realizing it. This is truly lamentable. Those who bear the responsibility of advocating for society should pay attention to this.

Gospel for Vocational Remedial Chinese Language 209

The local scholar Mr. Li Youzhi has been in the education field for more than 30 years. In view of the decline of Chinese studies, he founded a Chinese language night school four years ago in the Zhiming School on the west end of Hongqiao in Nanshi, specializing in remedial applied writing for those with jobs. The time is from 6:00 to 7:00 PM for higher-level classes and from 7:00 to 8:00 PM for general classes. At the beginning of each semester, the number of students reaches 100. Latecomers often regret being turned away due to full enrollment. This semester is the seventh time for enrollment (both men and women are accepted). Classes are scheduled to start on August 24th. Currently, Mr. Li's students Yan Duhe, Zhang Gongquan, Wu Yunzhu, Chen Jicheng, and others are introducing it.

Drowning in Cold Water Bath 210

Xu Jinlong, a Yangzhou native who opened a steamed bun shop at No. 1405 Dixiwei Road, was 24 years old. Due to the excessively hot weather recently, he went to take a cold water bath in the Zhonghongqiao River at 7:10 PM last night. However, Xu was very familiar with water and had excellent results. However, not long after entering the water, he somehow drowned. The patrolman found him and quickly tried to retrieve the body. Beggar Slashes Throat 211

A group of beggars often lived in Laotaiping Middle Alley in the Shiliupu area. At 4:00 PM the day before yesterday, a beggar, about 30 years old, with his upper body bare and wearing only a pair of black gauze pants, slashed his throat with a razor. Blood flowed like a stream. A police officer from the ninth post discovered it and immediately had the Red Cross branch sew up the wound. While he was being treated, he died because his throat was severed. Yesterday, the police station of the first district ordered the local leader Lu Yongde to report to the local court for an examination.

Daylight Robbery on Xietu Road 212

Wang Yaogen, a local resident living at No. 2471 Wangjiatang, Xietu Road, Shanghai West, is currently a foreman in the French Engineering Bureau and an honorary member of the first platoon of the tenth team of the South Shanghai District Security Corps. He has two self-provided handguns and one rifle at home. He built a house last autumn and is a moderately well-off family. Recently, robbers coveted him. At about 11:00 AM yesterday, seven robbers speaking mixed accents suddenly came. Two robbers stood guard at the gate, and five robbers entered to rob. Two of them were wearing Western suits, and three had handguns. Wang was out and had not returned. Wang's wife, Yang, and others were confined to one room. The robbers went upstairs to search and robbed 50 silver dollars, a gold watch, two gold rings, and dozens of men's and women's silk clothes. They also took a Type 38 rifle out of the door and threw it in the vegetable garden behind the house. Fortunately, the two handguns were not taken away. After about 40 minutes, they walked east towards Jinji Bridge. The victim has now issued a loss list and reported it to the second branch of the sixth district of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, requesting investigation and handling.

Worker Electrocuted to Death 213

Wang Chengzhi, a native of Zhenjiang, 29 years old, was a craftsman at the Pudong Electric Company. At 5:00 PM the day before yesterday, he was repairing electrical wires near Gaomu Bridge on the east end of Lujiazui. At that time, he was working high on the utility pole, but due to a moment of carelessness, he was suddenly electrocuted to death. His body remained suspended on the pole. After someone found a way to lower it, the Public Security Bureau of the third district ordered the local guarantor Xie Along to report to the court for an examination yesterday morning. In the afternoon, Prosecutor Yang led a team to the scene and confirmed that it was an electrocution. He instructed that the body be handed over to the family for burial.

Three-Year-Old Child Run Over by Car 214

At about 3:00 PM the day before yesterday, near the Jin Situ Temple on Kangnaoduo Road in Shanghai West, Xu Degui's son, Xiaomao, who was only three years old, was walking and playing on the side of the road. Suddenly, a large truck with Concession Certificate No. 9488 and Municipal Government Certificate No. 3419 came speeding from east to west. Due to a moment of carelessness, the child was knocked down and run over. A police officer stepped forward, but the driver immediately sped away. The police then chased after him, blowing the whistle frantically. Fortunately, the patrol officer stopped the car and the driver, Zhang Hongsheng.

Detained at the Gordon Road Police Station. The police then took the injured child back to the sixth district police station to report. He was immediately sent to the Red Cross Hospital for treatment. Due to the severity of his injuries, he died soon after. Subsequently, Cai, the district officer of the sixth district, and Police Chief Yang went to investigate. It was confirmed that the death was due to serious injuries.

Free Talk

One Branch of Tan

Strength and Softness 228

— Zhan Lu

The person who has entered the academy says a word to console himself, which is: Softness can overcome strength. This is because he was poisoned by Lao Tzu. Lao Tzu saw the tongue and thought that softness was good, and saw the teeth and thought that strength was not good. He said: The teeth are strong and firm, and will fail first; the tongue is soft, and therefore survives.

Later generations extended its meaning, thinking that the tongue is often insulted by the teeth; if it is accidentally chewed by the teeth, the tongue does not dare to resist. However, over time, these thirty-six dental generals will inevitably die in battle one after another, but this non-resisting tongue will be unharmed until old age, which is called softness can overcome strength.

Alas! I don't think so. I only heard the teeth chewing off the tip of the tongue, and did not hear the tip of the tongue picking off the teeth. I only hear the quick knife cutting tofu, with both sides smooth; I don't hear that buying a piece of tofu can really be used to kill yourself on it. Strength can overcome softness is common; softness can overcome strength is just the weak eating a pill of peace of mind there.

The wounds of Shanghai and Songhu have not yet recovered, and the situation in North China is urgent again! Are our military authorities acting as tongues? Or teeth?

History tells me that the Han and Tang Dynasties advocated strength against foreigners, and although the Han and Tang Dynasties have passed, the names of Han people and Tang people still exist today; the Song Dynasty advocated softness against foreigners, and later generations called them Song Snot. If we insist on non-resistance, after Song Snot, there will be People's Snot!

Even if softness can overcome strength is effective, when softness can no longer be soft, it is better to be a shattered jade than a whole tile.

Occasionally reading Mr. Hong Beijiang's article on strength and softness, he also said: Even if it is said that softness can overcome strength, I would rather be a broken Longquan Tai'a sword than to survive as a wandering vine and tendrils.

Japanese Silk Weaving of Manchurian-Mongolian Handkerchiefs 229

— Mao Fangmei

Yesterday I visited the art exhibition of the Chinese Society of Arts and Sciences. In the exhibition room of Shen Bao Photography Society's exhibits, I saw a Japanese-made silk handkerchief. It is collected by Mr. Li Yintan. It details the maps of Fengtian, Jilin, Heilongjiang, Rehe, and Outer Mongolia provinces. Separated from Japan by the sea. The provinces of Fengtian and Jilin are the most detailed. The dangers of Lushun and Weihaiwei. The repairs of Yingkou and Shanhaiguan. It is clear at a glance.

At the bottom of the handkerchief. Attached is a list of Manchuria and Mongolia. Signed Showa Five

Year. It states the area (Four Eastern Provinces) of 656,000 square miles. Population of 33.7 million. 13 million cho of cultivated land. Agricultural products of approximately 1.3 billion yen. 220,000 Japanese (including affiliated territories).

We can see from this that the Japanese want to seize Manchuria and Mongolia. Its premeditation. All-pervasive. Even the slightest handkerchief. We must also link the maps of Manchuria and Mongolia with Japan on it. It can be said that it has exhausted the ability to invade. I have heard that Japanese elementary school students. Regarding the area, population, terrain, climate, products, transportation, etc. of Manchuria and Mongolia. They can all be known like the back of their hand. But we Chinese citizens. On the contrary, I feel at a loss. I studied this handkerchief three times. Really ashamed.

Suzhou in Summer 231

— Zhu Wei

The Red Emperor holds sway, and the scorching sun unleashes its might. Even in this blistering summer, there are notable events in Suzhou society. I write this while wiping away sweat, to truly speak freely.

The lotus blooms in summer, its redness enchanting and its whiteness translucent, hidden amongst the lush green canopy. Its fragrance spreads far and wide, its charm especially abundant. Among the places where lotuses grow in Suzhou, Huangtiandang in Panxi should be considered foremost. For ten miles, the green canopy extends. One can take a small boat early in the morning or at dusk, and drift in the middle of the stream, enveloped in fragrance. Alas, today there is a lack of people with the refined interest to bring famous flowers and fine wine, going to appreciate the lotus. Among the gardens in the city that have lotus ponds, the Humble Administrator's Garden and the Retreat and Enjoy Garden are the most famous. The Retreat and Enjoy Garden is not open these days. The Humble Administrator's Garden is also lacking in fine breeds, due to years of disrepair. The lotuses in the parks have recently become abundant. The three lotus ponds stand tall and lush, following the rise of the two gardens. However, as visitors to the parks are busy reveling in the beauty of face powder and rouge, how many can truly appreciate the pure charm of the lotus pond? It calls for a sigh.

As the scorching heat intensifies, the number of people catching the epidemic increases daily. The epidemic hospitals are constantly reporting that they are full. Therefore, the people of Suzhou, who have always valued superstition, are competing to raise funds to perform public rituals to protect the region and drive away the epidemic. The lives of Daoist priests have become extremely busy. Every day, as the setting sun approaches, the Daoist priests in the Sanqing Hall of the Xuanmiao Temple offer up oblations multiple times a day. Their attire is magnificent, and the flute music is melodious, arousing endless feelings of wonder. Recently, the Temple of the Plague General was the scene of a strange incident where police officers broke into the premises because the temple did not comply with the government's ban on public gatherings. This is truly a strange phenomenon in broad daylight.

The great Yellow Register Ritual for Rain that was performed at the Sanqing Hall ended the other day. As a result, a light rain fell. Unfortunately, the two brief showers quickly gave way to sunshine, truly proving the saying, "The rain you pray for is never much." However, superstitious people deeply believe in the boundless power of the Daoist priests. How laughable it is!

Qizi Mountain, outside Xumen Gate, sees its pilgrimage season on the first and fifteenth days of the seventh month. As early as the fifth day of the seventh month, more than a thousand devout men and women of the Three Elders Society of the Xuanmiao Temple went up the mountain to offer incense. During the day, they climbed the mountain, rushing between the scorching sun and burning incense candles. In the evening, when they descended, they indulged in rich food and wine. (The meals of those who go to Qizi Mountain consist of vegetarian food on the way up, and meat on the way down.) I, Zhu Wei, am not wise, and I sincerely fear that such superstitious behavior will cause them to seek blessings only to bring misfortune upon themselves.

A Brief Discussion on Seasonal Illnesses 232

— Wang Qiangcheng

The scorching sun hangs high, and the fierce heat is intense. During this hot summer, we often seek coolness to escape the heat, which can easily lead to illness. If one can eat less raw, cold, greasy food and sleep with clothes on, external evils will have no way to invade. Even if one becomes ill, it will be mild and easily treated. This year, the weather is abnormal. There was excessive rainfall during the plum rain season, and the climate was cold. Since the beginning of summer, it has been unusually hot and humid. As a result, many people eat raw, cold fruits and vegetables, and sleep with windows open, indulging in temporary comfort. Wind and cold thus invade, and dampness takes the opportunity to strike, causing a buildup. This leads to this ailment. In mild cases, it lasts two to three weeks, and in severe cases, two to three months. Dampness is sticky, and not easily dispelled quickly. Treatment should be gradual and not rushed. At the beginning of this illness, one can use medicines that dry dampness, such as Magnolia bark and Atractylodes lancea. But after a period of time, white rashes and red eruptions appear one after another. (At this time, the utmost caution is required. The danger to life lies in whether the eruptions are released smoothly or not.) This is a sign that the evil dampness is being released externally. It is crucial not to administer cold medicines, which would prevent the rashes and eruptions from spreading smoothly. It is also not advisable to use warming and drying agents. At this stage, one should avoid drying medicines to prevent injury to yin. How could one use warming and drying agents again? One must be cautious in this hot weather. I recall that last year, my friend Mr. Wang Feilong also suffered from this illness. Dangerous situations arose repeatedly. Whenever I went to treat him, my teacher always told me to use less warming and hot medicines, for fear of depleting yin fluids. The illness gradually healed after a month. (My esteemed teacher has considerable experience with this ailment.) A certain famous doctor in Shanghai, upon seeing cold limbs, assumed it was a deficiency of yang. He prescribed warming and hot medicines such as aconite, cinnamon, and roasted ginger, leading to a fatal outcome. Such cases are not uncommon. In cases of damp-heat disease, cold hands and feet are due to heat being trapped in dampness. Clear yang cannot be spread. If one uses light and clear methods to unblock, the limbs will become warm again. Those who practice medicine must be extremely cautious. (Respectful payment.)

A Record of the Zhenhai Warship's Southern Voyage 233

— Lu Jingqing

The Zhenhai warship is directly under the command of the Bohai Fleet. It has recently made a grand tour of the South Seas, marking the first time a Chinese warship has sailed to Taiwan. This voyage was made without external authorization, which can be considered an anomaly. It unexpectedly arrived in Songbin the other day, also marking its first visit to Shanghai. The captain, Sheng Jianji (erroneously reported as his brother Jianxun), is an accomplished individual in his prime. He hails from Nanhui, and is a fellow乡党. From a young age, he was spirited and determined. He devoted himself to his studies, emulating Zu Ti's striking the oar and admiring Zong Que's ambition. He first studied at the Yantai Naval Academy, and then graduated from the Jinling Naval Academy. He immersed himself in military texts, spending years in diligent study. With the talent of a scholar and the perseverance of a soldier, he is highly respected by his peers. He has been the captain of the Zhenhai warship for many years. Recently, the naval students of the warship have been practicing navigation. They set sail from Qingdao in late June, passing through the sea ports of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Fujian, and Guangdong. Although they encountered rain, wind, raging tides and towering waves, they navigated the dangers with ease and have now announced their return. How joyful it is to know that the great peng bird has flown ten thousand miles with sails unharmed. Yesterday morning, I went to the naval dock at Gaochang Temple. I boarded the warship's private steam boat and, upon boarding the ship, shook hands with Captain Sheng and greeted him. We had a pleasant conversation about our shared hometown. I was treated to a lavish banquet, showing a deep friendship. Captain Sheng said that there are currently only three naval academies in the country: Weihaiwei, Mawei, and Huangpu. The Mawei Naval Academy is relatively complete. Before the Zhili-Fengtian War, Qingdao only had three military ships. Now there are a total of ten. Compared to the powerful warships of the other powers, it is like wearing tattered clothes and standing with those dressed in fox and badger fur, feeling ashamed of falling behind and having no place to hide. The longer a country's coastline, the more difficult it is to equip its navy. Countries are judged by the number of their warships. Evaluating our country's warships, it is only a comforting gesture. The situation is already shifting from black to white, and the trend is turning from green to yellow. The urgent task at present is to emphasize industry in order to enrich the people. If we can devote ourselves to the manufacturing of the steel industry and increase various types of production, in order to enrich people's livelihood, then the revitalization of the army and navy will be easy, and the foundation of the country can be strengthened. On the contrary, only focusing on increasing the military strength of a certain aspect is enough to harm the people, and the drawbacks are unbearable to speak of. This time, when the warship arrived at the port of Keelung in Taiwan, the overseas Chinese were overjoyed and warmly welcomed it, just like the Crusaders seeing Jerusalem. They then visited the museum, the Governor-General's Office, and various newspaper offices, and met with the Chinese Consul Yuan Jiada and the Governor-General of Taiwan, Suzuki, and naval officers. Then, the Secretary of the Bingshan Section was sent by Governor-General Zhongchuan to visit the Chinese Consulate in return, and also attended a welcome banquet at the Chinese General Chamber of Commerce. After inspecting the ports, there were many感慨. According to records, the people of Taiwan had been forced to change their nationality to Japanese before the Sino-Japanese War of 1894-1895. After the Sino-Japanese War, about 60,000 overseas Chinese went to Taiwan. The Japanese government imposed strict restrictions, especially towards the educated class. Most of those who went to Taiwan were laborers such as coal miners, barbers, and servants. Each port has an overseas Chinese association, with the general association located in Taipei. Only last year was a consul established. Chinese people are prohibited from establishing schools and newspapers there. Books sent from China are confiscated by customs. Overseas Chinese are trapped in the legal net, often being oppressed. The tragedy of a lost country is so cruel. Therefore, all overseas Chinese eagerly hope for the prosperity of their motherland. As they were about to leave, they all felt悲凉. They went to Dapeng Bay and felt it had great potential, but it has become a den of thieves, which is regrettable. The pleasant conversation unknowingly passed the time. Then, they visited the wireless telegraph room, the engine room, and the map room. The ship's navigator, Mr. Fang, said that the military maps printed in England are the best. The maps printed in Taiwan are mostly translated from English ones. China lacks anything comparable. In the center of the ship, there is a reading room, stocked with the Complete Library of Four Treasures and various magazines. The shelves are lined with books. Every department felt that the layout was neat and orderly. The soldiers were well-organized, polite, and knew etiquette. Then, I boarded a steam boat with Captain Sheng to return to shore and bid farewell. He said that they planned to leave Shanghai within a few days, and would avoid the scorching sun of the mainland by sailing at sea. The departure is no different from ascending to heaven. A farewell to the Shanghai waves, I don't know when we will meet again.

Gold Price Drops Five Taels and Eight Mace 234

Extreme Volatility The gold market experienced extreme volatility yesterday, with wild fluctuations that seemed unstoppable, rising and falling as if in a fog. There was a difference of over ten taels between the morning and afternoon, causing great anxiety and making predictions difficult. Ultimately, the price continued to fall by around six taels. Reports from the trading floor indicated strong buying by the US to maintain the international financial situation, leading to a decline in the Shanghai market. After opening lower, the price quickly broke 730 taels, greatly shocking the bulls. The Guangdong traders also showed a tendency to sell. Due to the severe shortage of foreign exchange, the market experienced a rapid decline of over ten taels, eventually breaking 720 taels. Subsequently, the exchange rate seemed to stabilize, and banks showed good buying interest, causing those who had sold in the morning to buy back. Short sellers who had profited also took the opportunity to cover their positions, leading to a sudden surge in the market, with a rebound of ten taels. The rebound was quite volatile. Later, the price settled around 728 taels. As it was Wednesday, and the hot weather persisted, the market was closed for half a day. Here is a recap of the morning's activity.

Status of New Cotton Crop in Tongzhou 244

Reduced Cotton Fields by 10-20%; New Cotton Conditions Favorable

The following is a second estimate of this year's cotton production and acreage in Tongzhou, as released by a foreign firm:

| | |

| :------------------------------------------------------------------ | :-------------------------- |

| Due to severe flood damage last year and the low price of cotton relative to rice, this year's acreage is estimated to have decreased by about 20%. Despite excessive rainfall around planting time, conditions have been favorable since then, leading to healthy cotton plant development. Yields are expected to be at or above normal. The following is a breakdown of cotton acreage in Tongzhou: | |

| (Nantong County): Last year's severe floods resulted in a harvest of only 20% of normal, with an average yield of 26 jin of seed cotton per mu. Due to the impact of falling imported cotton prices, about 45% of this year's crops are cotton, and 55% are grains. Cotton acreage is down 20% from last year. Weather conditions have been favorable since planting, and cotton plant development has been good. In the worst-affected areas, cotton plants are over six inches tall, and in Xiangqiaoan, they reach 1.5 feet. | |

| (Haimen County): Last year's harvest was relatively good, but still only yielded 30% of normal, with a yield of no more than 40 jin of seed cotton per mu. This year's cotton acreage is down about 15% from last year, with cotton and grains each accounting for about half of the crops. Growing conditions are better than in Nantong, and yields are expected to be about 80% of normal. | |

| (Rugao County): Last year suffered the most severe flood damage, especially in Matang and Chahe, where yields were minimal, only 10% of normal. The county-wide average was only 15%. This year's cotton acreage is down about 25% from last year, with a 4:6 ratio of cotton to grains. Weather conditions have been favorable since planting, and plant development has been good, with cotton plants averaging 8-9 inches tall. Yields are expected to be 80% or more of normal. | |

Grain: Old Rice Prices Fall by 0.2-0.3 Silver Dollars 246

South Shanghai 247

Yesterday, the number of incoming shipments from various suppliers was limited, approximately twenty. Sales in urban and rural stores were poor, and the Zha market weakened first, followed by a general decline. As a result, thick and thin japonica rice prices fell by 0.2-0.3 silver dollars, and early rice also fell by almost 0.1 silver dollar. Foreign Dudu sharp goods were slow to sell, and the market weakened. Bianyin yuan was short of goods. 700 shi of Zhoupu new japonica rice arrived. The opening price was fixed.

Xin Zha 248

Yesterday, there were about sixteen or seventeen shipments from the western route. Customer demand was non-existent. Scattered trading amounted to around 1,000 shi. In the morning opening, Changxi northern japonica rice fell by a small amount. Qingjiao, Shipu, Jiashan, and other early and late rice varieties saw no gains or losses. Bianyuan rice porters saw slight movement, with prices being tight. New japonica rice prices were similar to those in the South Shanghai market.

Imported Rice Recovers Slightly by 0.05 Silver Dollars 249

Imported rice prices slightly improved yesterday. Northern buyers inquired about Saigon rice, and Jiangbei and inland merchants arranged for the shipment of small-sized ground rice. While Hunan rice could be exported, the combined price was quite high, leading to optimistic sentiment. Prices recovered by 0.05 silver dollars compared to the previous session. High-quality small-sized ground rice was priced at up to 9.80 silver dollars, while ordinary rice was priced at 9.60-9.70 silver dollars. Old small-sized ground rice was priced at 9.35 silver dollars. A total of 5,000 bags were traded, including 2,000 bags of Saigon rice priced at 10.225-10.25 silver dollars. Except for 500 bags purchased by northern buyers, all Saigon rice was purchased by merchants in this street. Jiangbei and inland merchants arranged for the shipment of 2,500 bags of small-sized ground rice, with the remainder also being purchased by merchants in this street.

Wheat Flour Futures Plunge by 0.03-0.04 Silver Dollars 250

Yesterday, the wheat flour market saw a sharp decline across all months after the morning opening. Foreign wheat quotations fell by 0.4-0.6 silver dollars. Extended foreign exchange rates and plummeting gold prices made it opportune for foreign wheat to enter China. At yesterday's highest exchange rate, the price of foreign wheat was only 4.0 taels. The market was unstable from the opening, effectively falling by 0.02-0.03 silver dollars from the previous day. Subsequent selling from factories like Fufu further dampened the market. Distant months were even more sensitive due to rumors about foreign wheat. Northern and Southern foreign buyers made minor purchases, but were unable to counteract the trend. As a result, the current month fell by 0.0275 silver dollars, September fell by 0.0325 silver dollars, October fell by 0.0375 silver dollars, November and December fell by 0.0425 silver dollars, and January fell by 0.04 silver dollars.

Wheat Futures Follow Foreign Wheat Lower 251

But the decline was small

Yesterday's wheat futures market saw a uniform decline across all months after the morning opening, with foreign wheat quotations falling by 0.4-0.5 silver dollars. Rumors of foreign wheat being traded at 9.5 mace were likely untrue. However, due to the extended exchange rate, peddling of foreign wheat was very active, and factories were constantly inquiring, which unnerved the market. However, due to the persistent drought, domestic sentiment remained bullish, so while the market declined, the magnitude was small. As a result, the current month fell by 0.03 silver dollars, and September through December each fell by 0.04 silver dollars. Spot wheat remained firm, with Suqian wheat priced at 3.6 taels, Yaowan wheat at 3.6 taels, Zhenjiang wheat at 3.42 taels, and Anting wheat at 3.32 taels, totaling over 1,300 bags.
